We consider the regression problem рқҗІ=MвҖӢрқҗұ+ПөрқҗІрқ‘Җрқҗұitalic-Пө\mathbf{y}=M\mathbf{x}+\epsilon in the highdimensional setting, where рқҗұвҲҲрқҗ‘d1рқҗұsuperscriptрқҗ‘subscriptрқ‘‘1\mathbf{x}\in\mathbf{R}^{d_{1}} is the vector of features,рқҗІвҲҲрқҗ‘d2рқҗІsuperscriptрқҗ‘subscriptрқ‘‘2\mathbf{y}\in\mathbf{R}^{d_{2}} is a vector of responses, MвҲҲрқҗ‘d2Г—d1рқ‘Җsuperscriptрқҗ‘subscriptрқ‘‘2subscriptрқ‘‘1M\in\mathbf{R}^{d_{2}\times d_{1}} are the learnable parameters, and ПөвҲјNвҖӢ(0,ПғПө2вҖӢId2Г—d2)similar-toitalic-Пөрқ‘Ғ0subscriptsuperscriptрқңҺ2italic-Пөsubscriptрқҗјsubscriptрқ‘‘2subscriptрқ‘‘2\epsilon\sim N(0,\sigma^{2}_{\epsilon}I_{d_{2}\times d_{2}}) is a noise term.High-dimensional setting refers to the case where the number of observationsnрқ‘ӣn is insufficient for recovery andhence regularization for estimation isnecessaryВ koltchinskii2011nuclear ; negahban2011estimation ; chen2013reduced .This high-dimensional model is widely used in practice, such as identifyingbiomarkersВ zhu2017low , understanding risks associated with variousdiseasesВ frank2015dietary ; batis2016using , imagerecognitionВ rahim2017multi ; fan2017hyperspectral , forecasting equityreturns in financialmarketsВ polk2006cross ; stock2011dynamic ; medeiros2012estimating ; bender2013foundations ,and analyzing social networksВ wu2017generalized ; ralescu2011spectral .

We consider the вҖңlarge feature sizeвҖқ setting, in which the number of features d1subscriptрқ‘‘1d_{1}is excessively large and can be even larger than the number of observations nрқ‘ӣn. This setting frequently arises in practice because it is often straightforward to perform feature-engineering and produce a large number of potentially useful features in many machine learning problems. For example, in a typical equity forecasting model, nрқ‘ӣn is around 3,000 (i.e., using 10 years of market data), whereas the number of potentially relevant features can be in the order of thousandsВ polk2006cross ; gu2018empirical ; kelly2019characteristics ; chen2019deep . In predicting the popularity of a user in an online social network, nрқ‘ӣn is in the order of hundreds (each day is an observation and a typical dataset contains less than three years of data) whereas the feature size can easily be more than 10kВ ravikumar2010high ; bamman2014gender ; sinha2013predicting .

Existing low-rank regularization techniques (e.g.,В koltchinskii2011nuclear ; negahban2011estimation ; ma2014adaptive ) are not optimized for the large feature size setting. These results assume that either the features possess the so-called restricted isometry propertyВ candes2008restricted ,or their covariance matrix can be accurately estimatedВ negahban2011estimation . Therefore, their sample complexity nрқ‘ӣn dependson either d1subscriptрқ‘‘1d_{1} or the smallest eigenvalue value О»minsubscriptрқңҶ\lambda_{\min} of рқҗұрқҗұ\mathbf{x}вҖҷs covariance matrix. For example, a mean-squared error (MSE) result that appeared inВ negahban2011estimation is of the formOвҖӢ(rвҖӢ(d1+d2)nвҖӢО»min2)рқ‘Ӯрқ‘ҹsubscriptрқ‘‘1subscriptрқ‘‘2рқ‘ӣsubscriptsuperscriptрқңҶ2O\left(\frac{r(d_{1}+d_{2})}{n\lambda^{2}_{\min}}\right).WhennвүӨd1/О»min2рқ‘ӣsubscriptрқ‘‘1subscriptsuperscriptрқңҶ2n\leq d_{1}/\lambda^{2}_{\min},this result becomes trivial because the forecast рқҗІ^=рқҹҺ^рқҗІ0\hat{\mathbf{y}}=\mathbf{0} produces a comparable MSE. We design an efficient algorithm for the large feature size setting. Our algorithm is a simple two-stage algorithm. Let рқҗ—вҲҲрқҗ‘nГ—d1рқҗ—superscriptрқҗ‘рқ‘ӣsubscriptрқ‘‘1\mathbf{X}\in\mathbf{R}^{n\times d_{1}} be a matrix that stacks together all features and рқҗҳвҲҲрқҗ‘nГ—d2рқҗҳsuperscriptрқҗ‘рқ‘ӣsubscriptрқ‘‘2\mathbf{Y}\in\mathbf{R}^{n\times d_{2}} be the one that stacks the responses. In the first stage, we run a principal component analysis (PCA) on рқҗ—рқҗ—\mathbf{X} to obtain a set of uncorrelated features рқҗҷ^^рқҗҷ\hat{\mathbf{Z}}. In the second stage, we run another PCA to obtain a low rank approximation of рқҗҷ^TвҖӢрқҗҳsuperscript^рқҗҷTрқҗҳ\hat{\mathbf{Z}}^{\mathrm{T}}\mathbf{Y} and use it to construct an output.

While the algorithm is operationally simple, we show a powerful and generic result on using PCA to process features, a widely used practice for вҖңdimensionality reductionвҖқВ cao2003comparison ; ghodsi2006dimensionality ; friedman2001elements . PCA is known to be effective to orthogonalize features by keepingonly the subspace explaining large variations. But its performance can only be analyzed under the so-called factor modelВ stock2002forecasting ; stock2011dynamic . We show the efficacy of PCA without the factor model assumption.Instead, PCA should be interpreted as a robust estimator of рқҗұрқҗұ\mathbf{x}вҖҷs covariance matrix. The empirical estimator C=1nвҖӢрқҗ—рқҗ—Tрқҗ¶1рқ‘ӣsuperscriptрқҗ—рқҗ—TC=\frac{1}{n}\mathbf{X}\mathbf{X}^{\mathrm{T}} in the high-dimensional setting cannot be directly used because nвүӘd1Г—d2much-less-thanрқ‘ӣsubscriptрқ‘‘1subscriptрқ‘‘2n\ll d_{1}\times d_{2}, but it exhibits an interesting regularity: the leading eigenvectors of Cрқҗ¶C are closer to ground truth than the remaining ones. In addition,the number of reliable eigenvectors grows as the sample size grows, so our PCA procedureprojects the features along reliable eigenvectors anddynamically adjusts рқҗҷ^^рқҗҷ\hat{\mathbf{Z}}вҖҷs rank to maximally utilize the raw features.Under mild conditions on the ground-truth covariance matrix CвҲ—superscriptрқҗ¶C^{*} of рқҗұрқҗұ\mathbf{x}, we show that it is always possible to decompose рқҗұрқҗұ\mathbf{x} into a set of near-independent features and a set of (discarded) features that have an inconsequential impact on a modelвҖҷs MSE.

When features рқҗұрқҗұ\mathbf{x} are transformed into uncorrelated ones рқҗірқҗі\mathbf{z}, our original problem becomes рқҗІ=NвҖӢрқҗі+ПөрқҗІрқ‘Ғрқҗіitalic-Пө\mathbf{y}=N\mathbf{z}+\epsilon, which can be reduced to a matrix denoising problemВ donoho2014minimax  and be solved by the second stage.Our algorithm guarantees that we can recover all singular vectors of Nрқ‘ҒN whose associated singular values are larger than a certain threshold П„рқңҸ\tau. The performance guarantee can be translated into MSE bounds parametrized by commonly used variables (though, these translations usually lead to looser bounds). For example, when Nрқ‘ҒNвҖҷs rank is rрқ‘ҹr, our result reducesthe MSE from OвҖӢ(rвҖӢ(d1+d2)nвҖӢО»min2)рқ‘Ӯрқ‘ҹsubscriptрқ‘‘1subscriptрқ‘‘2рқ‘ӣsubscriptsuperscriptрқңҶ2O(\frac{r(d_{1}+d_{2})}{n\lambda^{2}_{\min}}) toOвҖӢ(rвҖӢd2n+nвҲ’c)рқ‘Ӯрқ‘ҹsubscriptрқ‘‘2рқ‘ӣsuperscriptрқ‘ӣрқ‘җO(\frac{rd_{2}}{n}+n^{-c}) for a suitably small constant cрқ‘җc. The improvement is most pronounced when nвүӘd1much-less-thanрқ‘ӣsubscriptрқ‘‘1n\ll d_{1}.

We also provide a new matching lower bound. Our lower bound asserts that no algorithm can recover a fraction of singular vectors of Nрқ‘ҒN whose associated singular values are smaller than ПҒвҖӢП„рқңҢрқңҸ\rho\tau, where ПҒрқңҢ\rho is a вҖңgap parameterвҖқ. Our lower bound contribution is twofold. First, we introduce a notion of вҖңlocal minimaxвҖқ, which enables us to define a lower bound parametrized by the singular values of Nрқ‘ҒN. This is a stronger lower bound than those delivered by the standard minimax framework, which are often parametrized by the rank rрқ‘ҹr of Nрқ‘ҒNВ koltchinskii2011nuclear . Second, we develop a new probabilistic technique for establishing lower bounds under the new local minimax framework. Roughly speaking,our techniques assemble a large collection of matrices that share the same singular values of Nрқ‘ҒN but are far from each other, so no algorithm can successfully distinguish these matrices with identical spectra.

Notation.  Let рқҗ—вҲҲрқҗ‘nГ—d1рқҗ—superscriptрқҗ‘рқ‘ӣsubscriptрқ‘‘1\mathbf{X}\in\mathbf{R}^{n\times d_{1}} and рқҗҳвҲҲрқҗ‘nГ—d2рқҗҳsuperscriptрқҗ‘рқ‘ӣsubscriptрқ‘‘2\mathbf{Y}\in\mathbf{R}^{n\times d_{2}} be data matrices with their iрқ‘–i-th rows representing the iрқ‘–i-th observation.For matrix AрқҗҙA, we denoteits singular value decomposition as A=UAвҖӢОЈAвҖӢ(VA)Tрқҗҙsuperscriptрқ‘ҲрқҗҙsuperscriptОЈрқҗҙsuperscriptsuperscriptрқ‘үрқҗҙTA=U^{A}\Sigma^{A}(V^{A})^{\mathrm{T}} and рқҗҸrвҖӢ(A)вүңUrAвҖӢОЈrAвҖӢVrATвүңsubscriptрқҗҸрқ‘ҹрқҗҙsuperscriptsubscriptрқ‘Ҳрқ‘ҹрқҗҙsubscriptsuperscriptОЈрқҗҙрқ‘ҹsuperscriptsuperscriptsubscriptрқ‘үрқ‘ҹрқҗҙT\mathbf{P}_{r}(A)\triangleq U_{r}^{A}\Sigma^{A}_{r}{V_{r}^{A}}^{\mathrm{T}} is the rank rрқ‘ҹr approximation obtained bykeeping the top rрқ‘ҹr singular values and the corresponding singular vectors. When the context is clear, we drop the superscript AрқҗҙA and use U,ОЈ,рқ‘ҲОЈU,\Sigma, and Vрқ‘үV (Ursubscriptрқ‘Ҳрқ‘ҹU_{r}, ОЈrsubscriptОЈрқ‘ҹ\Sigma_{r}, and Vrsubscriptрқ‘үрқ‘ҹV_{r}) instead. Both ПғiвҖӢ(A)subscriptрқңҺрқ‘–рқҗҙ\sigma_{i}(A) and ПғiAsubscriptsuperscriptрқңҺрқҗҙрқ‘–\sigma^{A}_{i} are used to refer to iрқ‘–i-th singular value of AрқҗҙA.We use MATLAB notation when we refer to a specific row or column, e.g., V1,:subscriptрқ‘ү1:V_{1,:} is the first row of Vрқ‘үV and V:,1subscriptрқ‘ү:1V_{:,1} is the first column. вҖ–AвҖ–Fsubscriptnormрқҗҙрқҗ№\|A\|_{F}, вҖ–AвҖ–2subscriptnormрқҗҙ2\|A\|_{2}, and вҖ–AвҖ–вҲ—subscriptnormрқҗҙ\|A\|_{*} are Frobenius, spectral, and nuclear norms of AрқҗҙA. In general, we use boldface upper case (e.g., рқҗ—рқҗ—\mathbf{X}) to denote data matrices and boldface lower case (e.g., рқҗұрқҗұ\mathbf{x}) to denote one sample. Regular fonts denote other matrices. Let CвҲ—=IвҖӢEвҖӢ[рқҗұрқҗұT]superscriptрқҗ¶IEdelimited-[]superscriptрқҗұрқҗұTC^{*}=\mathrm{I\!E}[\mathbf{x}\mathbf{x}^{\mathrm{T}}] and C=1nвҖӢрқҗ—TвҖӢрқҗ—рқҗ¶1рқ‘ӣsuperscriptрқҗ—Tрқҗ—C=\frac{1}{n}\mathbf{X}^{\mathrm{T}}\mathbf{X} be the empirical estimate of CвҲ—superscriptрқҗ¶C^{*}. Let CвҲ—=VвҲ—вҖӢОӣвҲ—вҖӢ(VвҲ—)Tsuperscriptрқҗ¶superscriptрқ‘үsuperscriptОӣsuperscriptsuperscriptрқ‘үTC^{*}=V^{*}\Lambda^{*}(V^{*})^{\mathrm{T}} be the eigen-decomposition of the matrix CвҲ—superscriptрқҗ¶C^{*}, and О»1вҲ—вүҘО»2вҲ—,вҖҰ,вүҘО»d1вҲ—вүҘ0\lambda^{*}_{1}\geq\lambda^{*}_{2},\ldots,\geq\lambda^{*}_{d_{1}}\geq 0 be the diagonal entriesof ОӣвҲ—superscriptОӣ\Lambda^{*}. Let {рқҗ®1,рқҗ®2,вҖҰвҖӢрқҗ®в„“}subscriptрқҗ®1subscriptрқҗ®2вҖҰsubscriptрқҗ®в„“\{\mathbf{u}_{1},\mathbf{u}_{2},\dots\mathbf{u}_{\ell}\} be an arbitrary set of column vectors, and SpanвҖӢ({рқҗ®1,рқҗ®2,вҖҰ,рқҗ®в„“})Spansubscriptрқҗ®1subscriptрқҗ®2вҖҰsubscriptрқҗ®в„“\mathrm{Span}(\{\mathbf{u}_{1},\mathbf{u}_{2},\dots,\mathbf{u}_{\ell}\}) be the subspace spanned by it.An event happens with high probability means that it happens with probability вүҘ1вҲ’nвҲ’5absent1superscriptрқ‘ӣ5\geq 1-n^{-5}, where 5 is an arbitrarily chosen large constant and is not optimized.

Our model.  We consider the model рқҗІ=MвҖӢрқҗұ+ПөрқҗІрқ‘Җрқҗұitalic-Пө\mathbf{y}=M\mathbf{x}+\epsilon, where рқҗұвҲҲрқҗ‘d1рқҗұsuperscriptрқҗ‘subscriptрқ‘‘1\mathbf{x}\in\mathbf{R}^{d_{1}} is a multivariate Gaussian, рқҗІвҲҲрқҗ‘d2рқҗІsuperscriptрқҗ‘subscriptрқ‘‘2\mathbf{y}\in\mathbf{R}^{d_{2}}, MвҲҲрқҗ‘d2Г—d1рқ‘Җsuperscriptрқҗ‘subscriptрқ‘‘2subscriptрқ‘‘1M\in\mathbf{R}^{d_{2}\times d_{1}}, and ПөвҲјNвҖӢ(0,ПғПө2вҖӢId2Г—d2)similar-toitalic-Пөрқ‘Ғ0subscriptsuperscriptрқңҺ2italic-Пөsubscriptрқҗјsubscriptрқ‘‘2subscriptрқ‘‘2\epsilon\sim N(0,\sigma^{2}_{\epsilon}I_{d_{2}\times d_{2}}). We can relax the Gaussian assumptions on рқҗұрқҗұ\mathbf{x} and Пөitalic-Пө\epsilon for most results we develop. We assume a PAC learning framework, i.e., we observe a sequence {(рқҗұi,рқҗІi)}iвүӨnsubscriptsubscriptрқҗұрқ‘–subscriptрқҗІрқ‘–рқ‘–рқ‘ӣ\{(\mathbf{x}_{i},\mathbf{y}_{i})\}_{i\leq n} of independent samples and our goal is to find an M^^рқ‘Җ\hat{M} that minimizes the test error IвҖӢEрқҗұ,рқҗІвҖӢ[вҖ–M^вҖӢрқҗұвҲ’MвҖӢрқҗұвҖ–22]IsubscriptEрқҗұрқҗІdelimited-[]superscriptsubscriptnorm^рқ‘Җрқҗұрқ‘Җрқҗұ22\mathrm{I\!E}_{\mathbf{x},\mathbf{y}}[\|\hat{M}\mathbf{x}-M\mathbf{x}\|_{2}^{2}].We are specifically interested in the setting in which d2вүҲnвүӨd1subscriptрқ‘‘2рқ‘ӣsubscriptрқ‘‘1d_{2}\approx n\leq d_{1}.

The key assumption we make to circumvent the d1вүҘnsubscriptрқ‘‘1рқ‘ӣd_{1}\geq n issue is that the features are correlated. This assumption can be justified for the following reasons: (i) In practice, it is difficult, if not impossible,to construct completely uncorrelated features. (ii) When nвүӘd1much-less-thanрқ‘ӣsubscriptрқ‘‘1n\ll d_{1}, it is not even possible to test whether the features are uncorrelatedВ bai2010spectral .(iii) When we indeed know that the features are independent, there are significantly simpler methods to design models. For example, we can build multiple models such that each model regresses on an individual feature of рқҗұрқҗұ\mathbf{x}, and then use a boosting/bagging methodВ friedman2001elements ; schapire2013boosting  to consolidate the predictions.

The correlatedness assumption implies that the eigenvalues of CвҲ—superscriptрқҗ¶C^{*} decays. The only (full rank) positive semidefinite matrices that have non-decaying (uniform) eigenvalues are the identity matrix (up to some scaling). In other words, when CвҲ—superscriptрқҗ¶C^{*} has uniform eigenvalues, рқҗұрқҗұ\mathbf{x} has to be uncorrelated.

We aim to design an algorithm that works even when the decay is slow, such as when О»iвҖӢ(CвҲ—)subscriptрқңҶрқ‘–superscriptрқҗ¶\lambda_{i}(C^{*}) has a heavy tail. Specifically, our algorithm assumes О»isubscriptрқңҶрқ‘–\lambda_{i}вҖҷs are bounded by a heavy-tail power law series:

We do not make functional form assumptions on О»isubscriptрқңҶрқ‘–\lambda_{i}вҖҷs. This assumption also covers many benign cases, such as when CвҲ—superscriptрқҗ¶C^{*} has low rank or its eigenvalues decay exponentially. Many empirical studies report power law distributions of data covariance matricesВ akemann2010universal ; nobi2013random ; urama2017analysis ; clauset2009power . Next, we make standard normalization assumptions. IвҖӢEвҖӢвҖ–рқҗұвҖ–22=1IEsubscriptsuperscriptnormрқҗұ221\mathrm{I\!E}\|\mathbf{x}\|^{2}_{2}=1, вҖ–MвҖ–2вүӨОҘ=OвҖӢ(1)subscriptnormрқ‘Җ2ОҘрқ‘Ӯ1\|M\|_{2}\leq\Upsilon=O(1), and ПғПөвүҘ1subscriptрқңҺitalic-Пө1\sigma_{\epsilon}\geq 1.Remark that we assume only the spectral norm of Mрқ‘ҖM is bounded, while its Frobenius norm can be unbounded. Also, we assume the noise ПғПөвүҘ1subscriptрқңҺitalic-Пө1\sigma_{\epsilon}\geq 1 is sufficiently large, which is more important in practice. The case when ПғПөsubscriptрқңҺitalic-Пө\sigma_{\epsilon} is small can be tackled in a similar fashion.Finally, our studies avoid examining excessively unrealistic cases, so we assume d1вүӨd23subscriptрқ‘‘1subscriptsuperscriptрқ‘‘32d_{1}\leq d^{3}_{2}. We examinethe setting where existing algorithms fail to deliver non-trivial MSE, so we assume that nвүӨrвҖӢd1вүӨd24рқ‘ӣрқ‘ҹsubscriptрқ‘‘1subscriptsuperscriptрқ‘‘42n\leq rd_{1}\leq d^{4}_{2}.

Our algorithm (see Fig.В 1) consists of two steps.Step 1. Producing uncorrelated features.  We run a PCA to obtain a total number of k1subscriptрқ‘ҳ1k_{1} orthogonalized features. See \procвҖӢSвҖӢtвҖӢeвҖӢpвҲ’1вҲ’PвҖӢCвҖӢAвҲ’X\procрқ‘Ҷрқ‘Ўрқ‘’рқ‘қ1рқ‘ғрқҗ¶рқҗҙрқ‘Ӣ\proc{Step-1-PCA-X} in Fig.В 1. Let the SVD of рқҗ—рқҗ—\mathbf{X} be рқҗ—=UвҖӢОЈвҖӢ(V)Tрқҗ—рқ‘ҲОЈsuperscriptрқ‘үT\mathbf{X}=U\Sigma(V)^{\mathrm{T}}. Let k1subscriptрқ‘ҳ1k_{1} be a suitable rank chosen by inspecting the gaps of рқҗ—рқҗ—\mathbf{X}вҖҷs singular values (Line 5 in \procвҖӢSвҖӢtвҖӢeвҖӢpвҲ’1вҲ’PвҖӢCвҖӢAвҲ’X\procрқ‘Ҷрқ‘Ўрқ‘’рқ‘қ1рқ‘ғрқҗ¶рқҗҙрқ‘Ӣ\proc{Step-1-PCA-X}). рқҗҷ^+=nвҖӢUk1subscript^рқҗҷрқ‘ӣsubscriptрқ‘Ҳsubscriptрқ‘ҳ1\hat{\mathbf{Z}}_{+}=\sqrt{n}U_{k_{1}} is the set of transformed features output by this step. The subscript ++ in рқҗҷ^+subscript^рқҗҷ\hat{\mathbf{Z}}_{+} reflects that a dimension reduction happens so the number of columns in рқҗҷ^+subscript^рқҗҷ\hat{\mathbf{Z}}_{+} is smaller than that in рқҗ—рқҗ—\mathbf{X}. Compared to standard PCA dimension reduction, there are two differences: (i) We use the left leading singular vectors of рқҗ—рқҗ—\mathbf{X} (with a re-scaling factor nрқ‘ӣ\sqrt{n}) as the output, whereas the PCA reduction outputs рқҗҸk1вҖӢ(рқҗ—)subscriptрқҗҸsubscriptрқ‘ҳ1рқҗ—\mathbf{P}_{k_{1}}(\mathbf{X}). (ii) We design a specialized rule to choose k1subscriptрқ‘ҳ1k_{1} whereas PCA usually uses a hard thresholding or other ad-hoc rules.Step 2. Matrix denoising.  We run a second PCA on the matrix (N^+)Tвүң1nвҖӢрқҗҷ^+TвҖӢрқҗҳвүңsuperscriptsubscript^рқ‘ҒT1рқ‘ӣsuperscriptsubscript^рқҗҷTрқҗҳ(\hat{N}_{+})^{\mathrm{T}}\triangleq\frac{1}{n}\hat{\mathbf{Z}}_{+}^{\mathrm{T}}\mathbf{Y}. The rank k2subscriptрқ‘ҳ2k_{2} is chosen by a hard thresholding rule (Line 4 in \procвҖӢSвҖӢtвҖӢeвҖӢpвҲ’2вҲ’PвҖӢCвҖӢAвҲ’DвҖӢeвҖӢnвҖӢoвҖӢiвҖӢsвҖӢe\procрқ‘Ҷрқ‘Ўрқ‘’рқ‘қ2рқ‘ғрқҗ¶рқҗҙрқҗ·рқ‘’рқ‘ӣрқ‘ңрқ‘–рқ‘ рқ‘’\proc{Step-2-PCA-Denoise}). Our final estimator is рқҗҸk2вҖӢ(N^+)вҖӢО ^subscriptрқҗҸsubscriptрқ‘ҳ2subscript^рқ‘Ғ^О \mathbf{P}_{k_{2}}(\hat{N}_{+})\hat{\Pi}, where О ^=(Оӣk1)вҲ’12вҖӢVk1T^О superscriptsubscriptОӣsubscriptрқ‘ҳ112subscriptsuperscriptрқ‘үTsubscriptрқ‘ҳ1\hat{\Pi}=(\Lambda_{k_{1}})^{-\frac{1}{2}}V^{\mathrm{T}}_{k_{1}} is computed in \procвҖӢSвҖӢtвҖӢeвҖӢpвҲ’1вҲ’PвҖӢCвҖӢAвҲ’XвҖӢ(рқҗ—)\procрқ‘Ҷрқ‘Ўрқ‘’рқ‘қ1рқ‘ғрқҗ¶рқҗҙрқ‘Ӣрқҗ—\proc{Step-1-PCA-X}(\mathbf{X}).

While the algorithm is operationally simple, its design is motivated by carefully unfolding the statistical structure of the problem. We shall realize that applying PCA on the features should not be viewed as removing noise from a factor model, or finding subspaces that maximize variations explained by the subspaces as suggested in the standard literatureВ friedman2001elements ; stock2002forecasting ; stock2005implications .Instead, it implicitly implements a robust estimator for рқҗұрқҗұ\mathbf{x}вҖҷs precision matrix, and the design of the estimator needs to be coupled with our objective of forecasting рқҗІрқҗІ\mathbf{y}, thus resulting in a new way of choosing the rank.

Design motivation: warm up.  We first examine a simplified problem рқҗІ=NвҖӢрқҗі+ПөрқҗІрқ‘Ғрқҗіitalic-Пө\mathbf{y}=N\mathbf{z}+\epsilon, where variables in рқҗірқҗі\mathbf{z} are assumed to be uncorrelated. Assume d=d1=d2рқ‘‘subscriptрқ‘‘1subscriptрқ‘‘2d=d_{1}=d_{2}in this simplified setting. Observe that1nвҖӢрқҗҷTвҖӢрқҗҳ=1nвҖӢрқҗҷTвҖӢ(рқҗҷвҖӢNT+E)=(1nвҖӢрқҗҷTвҖӢрқҗҷ)вҖӢNT+1nвҖӢрқҗҷTвҖӢEвүҲId1Г—d1вҖӢNT+1nвҖӢрқҗҷTвҖӢE=NT+в„°,1рқ‘ӣsuperscriptрқҗҷTрқҗҳ1рқ‘ӣsuperscriptрқҗҷTрқҗҷsuperscriptрқ‘ҒTрқҗё1рқ‘ӣsuperscriptрқҗҷTрқҗҷsuperscriptрқ‘ҒT1рқ‘ӣsuperscriptрқҗҷTрқҗёsubscriptрқҗјsubscriptрқ‘‘1subscriptрқ‘‘1superscriptрқ‘ҒT1рқ‘ӣsuperscriptрқҗҷTрқҗёsuperscriptрқ‘ҒTв„°\displaystyle\frac{1}{n}\mathbf{Z}^{\mathrm{T}}\mathbf{Y}=\frac{1}{n}\mathbf{Z}^{\mathrm{T}}(\mathbf{Z}N^{\mathrm{T}}+E)=(\frac{1}{n}\mathbf{Z}^{\mathrm{T}}\mathbf{Z})N^{\mathrm{T}}+\frac{1}{n}\mathbf{Z}^{\mathrm{T}}E\approx I_{d_{1}\times d_{1}}N^{\mathrm{T}}+\frac{1}{n}\mathbf{Z}^{\mathrm{T}}E=N^{\mathrm{T}}+\mathcal{E},(1)where EрқҗёE is the noise term and в„°в„°\mathcal{E} can be approximated by a matrix with independent zero-mean noises.

Solving the matrix denoising problem.  Eq.В 1 implies that when we compute рқҗҷTвҖӢрқҗҳsuperscriptрқҗҷTрқҗҳ\mathbf{Z}^{\mathrm{T}}\mathbf{Y}, the problem reduces to an extensively studied matrix denoising problemВ donoho2014minimax ; gavish2014optimal .We include the intuition for solving this problem for completeness. The signal NTsuperscriptрқ‘ҒTN^{\mathrm{T}} is overlaidwith a noise matrix в„°в„°\mathcal{E}. в„°в„°\mathcal{E} will elevate all the singular values of NTsuperscriptрқ‘ҒTN^{\mathrm{T}} by an order of ПғПөвҖӢd/nsubscriptрқңҺitalic-Пөрқ‘‘рқ‘ӣ\sigma_{\epsilon}\sqrt{d/n}.We run a PCA to extract reliable signals:when the singular value of a subspace is вү«ПғПөвҖӢd/nmuch-greater-thanabsentsubscriptрқңҺitalic-Пөрқ‘‘рқ‘ӣ\gg\sigma_{\epsilon}\sqrt{d/n}, the subspace contains significantly more signal than noise and thus we keep the subspace. Similarly,a subspace associated a singular value вүІПғПөвҖӢd/nless-than-or-similar-toabsentsubscriptрқңҺitalic-Пөрқ‘‘рқ‘ӣ\lesssim\sigma_{\epsilon}\sqrt{d/n} mostly contains noise. This leads to a hard thresholding algorithm that setsN^T=рқҗҸrвҖӢ(NT+в„°)superscript^рқ‘ҒTsubscriptрқҗҸрқ‘ҹsuperscriptрқ‘ҒTв„°\hat{N}^{\mathrm{T}}=\mathbf{P}_{r}(N^{\mathrm{T}}+\mathcal{E}), where rрқ‘ҹr is the maximum index such that ПғrвҖӢ(NT+в„°)вүҘcвҖӢd/nsubscriptрқңҺрқ‘ҹsuperscriptрқ‘ҒTв„°рқ‘җрқ‘‘рқ‘ӣ\sigma_{r}(N^{\mathrm{T}}+\mathcal{E})\geq c\sqrt{d/n} for some constant cрқ‘җc. In the general setting рқҗІ=MвҖӢрқҗұ+ПөрқҗІрқ‘Җрқҗұitalic-Пө\mathbf{y}=M\mathbf{x}+\epsilon, рқҗұрқҗұ\mathbf{x} may not be uncorrelated. But when we set рқҗі=(ОӣвҲ—)вҲ’12вҖӢ(VвҲ—)TвҖӢрқҗұрқҗіsuperscriptsuperscriptОӣ12superscriptsuperscriptрқ‘үTрқҗұ\mathbf{z}=(\Lambda^{*})^{-\frac{1}{2}}(V^{*})^{\mathrm{T}}\mathbf{x}, we see that IвҖӢEвҖӢ[рқҗірқҗіT]=IIEdelimited-[]superscriptрқҗірқҗіTрқҗј\mathrm{I\!E}[\mathbf{z}\mathbf{z}^{\mathrm{T}}]=I. This means knowing CвҲ—superscriptрқҗ¶C^{*} suffices to reduce the original problem to a simplified one. Therefore, our algorithm uses Step 1 to estimate CвҲ—superscriptрқҗ¶C^{*} and рқҗҷрқҗҷ\mathbf{Z}, and uses Step 2 to reduce the problem to a matrix denoising one and solve it by standard thresholding techniques.

Relationship between PCA and precision matrix estimation.  In step 1, while we plan to estimate CвҲ—superscriptрқҗ¶C^{*}, our algorithm runs a PCA on рқҗ—рқҗ—\mathbf{X}.We observe that empirical covariance matrix C=1nвҖӢрқҗ—TвҖӢрқҗ—=1nвҖӢVвҖӢ(ОЈ)2вҖӢ(V)Tрқҗ¶1рқ‘ӣsuperscriptрқҗ—Tрқҗ—1рқ‘ӣрқ‘үsuperscriptОЈ2superscriptрқ‘үTC=\frac{1}{n}\mathbf{X}^{\mathrm{T}}\mathbf{X}=\frac{1}{n}V(\Sigma)^{2}(V)^{\mathrm{T}},i.e., Cрқҗ¶CвҖҷs eigenvectors coincide with рқҗ—рқҗ—\mathbf{X}вҖҷs right singular vectors. When we use the empirical estimator to construct рқҗі^^рқҗі\hat{\mathbf{z}}, we obtain рқҗі^=nвҖӢ(ОЈ)вҲ’1вҖӢ(V)TвҖӢрқҗұ^рқҗірқ‘ӣsuperscriptОЈ1superscriptрқ‘үTрқҗұ\hat{\mathbf{z}}=\sqrt{n}(\Sigma)^{-1}(V)^{\mathrm{T}}\mathbf{x}. When we apply this map to every training point and assemble the new feature matrix, we exactly getрқҗҷ^=nвҖӢрқҗ—вҖӢVвҖӢ(ОЈ)вҲ’1=nвҖӢU^рқҗҷрқ‘ӣрқҗ—рқ‘үsuperscriptОЈ1рқ‘ӣрқ‘Ҳ\hat{\mathbf{Z}}=\sqrt{n}\mathbf{X}V(\Sigma)^{-1}=\sqrt{n}U. It means that using Cрқҗ¶C to construct рқҗі^^рқҗі\hat{\mathbf{z}} is the same as running a PCA in \procвҖӢSвҖӢtвҖӢeвҖӢpвҲ’1вҲ’PвҖӢCвҖӢAвҲ’X\procрқ‘Ҷрқ‘Ўрқ‘’рқ‘қ1рқ‘ғрқҗ¶рқҗҙрқ‘Ӣ\proc{Step-1-PCA-X}with k1=d1subscriptрқ‘ҳ1subscriptрқ‘‘1k_{1}=d_{1}.

When k1<d1subscriptрқ‘ҳ1subscriptрқ‘‘1k_{1}<d_{1}, PCA uses a low rank approximation of Cрқҗ¶C as an estimator for CвҲ—superscriptрқҗ¶C^{*}. We now explain why this is effective. First, note that Cрқҗ¶C is very far from CвҲ—superscriptрқҗ¶C^{*} when nвүӘd1much-less-thanрқ‘ӣsubscriptрқ‘‘1n\ll d_{1}, therefore it is dangerous to directly plug in Cрқҗ¶C to find рқҗі^^рқҗі\hat{\mathbf{z}}. Second, an interesting regularity of Cрқҗ¶C exists and can be best explained by a picture. In Fig.В 2, we plot the pairwise anglesbetween eigenvectors of Cрқҗ¶C and those of CвҲ—superscriptрқҗ¶C^{*} from a synthetic dataset. Columns are sorted by the CвҲ—superscriptрқҗ¶C^{*}вҖҷs eigenvalues in decreasing order. When CвҲ—superscriptрқҗ¶C^{*} and Cрқҗ¶C coincide, this plot would look like an identity matrix. When Cрқҗ¶C and CвҲ—superscriptрқҗ¶C^{*} are unrelated, then the plot behaves like a block of white Gaussian noise. We observe a pronounced pattern: the angle matrix can be roughly divided into two sub-blocks (see the red lines in Fig.В 2). The upper left sub-block behaves like an identity matrix, suggesting that the leading eigenvectors of Cрқҗ¶C are close to those of CвҲ—superscriptрқҗ¶C^{*}. The lower right block behaves like a white noise matrix, suggesting that the вҖңsmallвҖқ eigenvectors of Cрқҗ¶C are far from those of CвҲ—superscriptрқҗ¶C^{*}. When nрқ‘ӣn grows, one can observe the upper left block becomes larger and this the eigenvectors of Cрқҗ¶C will sequentially get stabilized. Leading eigenvectors are first stabilized, followed by smaller ones.Our algorithm leverages this regularity by keeping only a suitable number of reliable eigenvectors from Cрқҗ¶C while ensuring not much information is lost when we throw away those вҖңsmallвҖқ eigenvectors.

Implementing the rank selection.  We rely on three interacting building blocks:

1. Dimension-free matrix concentration.  First, we need to find a concentration behavior of Cрқҗ¶C for nвүӨd1рқ‘ӣsubscriptрқ‘‘1n\leq d_{1} to decouple d1subscriptрқ‘‘1d_{1} from the MSE bound. We utilize adimension-free matrix concentration inequalityВ oliveira2010sums (also replicated as LemmaВ 3).Roughly speaking, the concentration behaves as вҖ–CвҲ’CвҲ—вҖ–2вүҲnвҲ’12subscriptnormрқҗ¶superscriptрқҗ¶2superscriptрқ‘ӣ12\|C-C^{*}\|_{2}\approx n^{-\frac{1}{2}}.This guarantees that |О»iвҖӢ(C)вҲ’О»iвҖӢ(CвҲ—)|вүӨnвҲ’12subscriptрқңҶрқ‘–рқҗ¶subscriptрқңҶрқ‘–superscriptрқҗ¶superscriptрқ‘ӣ12|\lambda_{i}(C)-\lambda_{i}(C^{*})|\leq n^{-\frac{1}{2}} by standard matrix perturbation resultsВ kato1987variation .

2. Davis-Kahan perturbation result.  However, the pairwise closeness of the О»isubscriptрқңҶрқ‘–\lambda_{i}вҖҷs does not imply the eigenvectors are also close.When О»iвҖӢ(CвҲ—)subscriptрқңҶрқ‘–superscriptрқҗ¶\lambda_{i}(C^{*}) and О»i+1вҖӢ(CвҲ—)subscriptрқңҶрқ‘–1superscriptрқҗ¶\lambda_{i+1}(C^{*}) are close, the corresponding eigenvectors in Cрқҗ¶C can be вҖңjammedвҖқ together. Thus, we need to identifyan index iрқ‘–i, at which О»iвҖӢ(CвҲ—)вҲ’О»i+1вҖӢ(CвҲ—)subscriptрқңҶрқ‘–superscriptрқҗ¶subscriptрқңҶрқ‘–1superscriptрқҗ¶\lambda_{i}(C^{*})-\lambda_{i+1}(C^{*}) exhibits significant gap, and use a Davis-Kahan result to show that рқҗҸiвҖӢ(C)subscriptрқҗҸрқ‘–рқҗ¶\mathbf{P}_{i}(C) is close to рқҗҸiвҖӢ(CвҲ—)subscriptрқҗҸрқ‘–superscriptрқҗ¶\mathbf{P}_{i}(C^{*}).On the other hand, the map О вҲ—(вүң(ОӣвҲ—)вҲ’12вҖӢ(VвҲ—)T)annotatedsuperscriptО вүңabsentsuperscriptsuperscriptОӣ12superscriptsuperscriptрқ‘үT\Pi^{*}(\triangleq(\Lambda^{*})^{-\frac{1}{2}}(V^{*})^{\mathrm{T}}) we aim to find depends on the square root of inverse (ОӣвҲ—)вҲ’12superscriptsuperscriptОӣ12(\Lambda^{*})^{-\frac{1}{2}}, so we needadditional manipulation to argue our estimate is close to (ОӣвҲ—)вҲ’12вҖӢ(VвҲ—)TsuperscriptsuperscriptОӣ12superscriptsuperscriptрқ‘үT(\Lambda^{*})^{-\frac{1}{2}}(V^{*})^{\mathrm{T}}.

3. The connection between gap and tail.  Finally, the performance of our procedureis also characterized by the total volume of signals that are discarded, i.e., вҲ‘i>k1О»iвҖӢ(CвҲ—)subscriptрқ‘–subscriptрқ‘ҳ1subscriptрқңҶрқ‘–superscriptрқҗ¶\sum_{i>k_{1}}\lambda_{i}(C^{*}), where k1subscriptрқ‘ҳ1k_{1} is the location that exhibits the gap.The question becomes whether it is possible to identify a k1subscriptрқ‘ҳ1k_{1} that simultaneously exhibits a large gap and ensures the tail after it is well-controlled, e.g., the sum of the tail is OвҖӢ(nвҲ’c)рқ‘Ӯsuperscriptрқ‘ӣрқ‘җO(n^{-c}) for a constant cрқ‘җc.We develop a combinatorial analysis to show that it is always possible to find such a gap under the assumption that О»iвҖӢ(CвҲ—)subscriptрқңҶрқ‘–superscriptрқҗ¶\lambda_{i}(C^{*}) is bounded by a power law distribution with exponent ПүвүҘ2рқң”2\omega\geq 2.Combining all these three building blocks, we have:

Prop.В 1 implies that our estimate рқҗі^+=О ^вҖӢ(рқҗұ)subscript^рқҗі^О рқҗұ\hat{\mathbf{z}}_{+}=\hat{\Pi}(\mathbf{x}) is sufficiently closeto рқҗі=О вҲ—вҖӢ(рқҗұ)рқҗіsuperscriptО рқҗұ\mathbf{z}=\Pi^{*}(\mathbf{x}), up to a unitary transform. We then execute \procвҖӢSвҖӢtвҖӢeвҖӢpвҲ’2вҲ’PвҖӢCвҖӢAвҲ’DвҖӢeвҖӢnвҖӢoвҖӢiвҖӢsвҖӢe\procрқ‘Ҷрқ‘Ўрқ‘’рқ‘қ2рқ‘ғрқҗ¶рқҗҙрқҗ·рқ‘’рқ‘ӣрқ‘ңрқ‘–рқ‘ рқ‘’\proc{Step-2-PCA-Denoise} to reduce the problem to a matrix denoising one and solve it by hard-thresholding.Let us refer to рқҗІ=NвҖӢрқҗі+ПөрқҗІрқ‘Ғрқҗіitalic-Пө\mathbf{y}=N\mathbf{z}+\epsilon, where рқҗірқҗі\mathbf{z} is a standard multivariate Gaussian and N=MвҖӢVвҲ—вҖӢ(ОӣвҲ—)12рқ‘Ғрқ‘Җsuperscriptрқ‘үsuperscriptsuperscriptОӣ12N=MV^{*}(\Lambda^{*})^{\frac{1}{2}} as the orthogonalized form of the problem.While we do not directly observe рқҗірқҗі\mathbf{z}, our performance is characterized by spectra structure of Nрқ‘ҒN.

TheoremВ 1 also implies that there exists a way to parametrize Оҫрқңү\xi and Оҙрқӣҝ\delta such thatIвҖӢEвҖӢ[вҖ–рқҗІ^вҲ’рқҗІвҖ–22]вүӨвҲ‘i>в„“вҲ—(ПғiN)2+OвҖӢ(в„“вҲ—вҖӢd2вҖӢОё2вҖӢПғПө2n)+OвҖӢ(nвҲ’c0)IEdelimited-[]subscriptsuperscriptnorm^рқҗІрқҗІ22subscriptрқ‘–superscriptв„“superscriptsubscriptsuperscriptрқңҺрқ‘Ғрқ‘–2рқ‘Ӯsuperscriptв„“subscriptрқ‘‘2superscriptрқңғ2subscriptsuperscriptрқңҺ2italic-Пөрқ‘ӣрқ‘Ӯsuperscriptрқ‘ӣsubscriptрқ‘җ0\mathrm{I\!E}[\|\hat{\mathbf{y}}-\mathbf{y}\|^{2}_{2}]\leq\sum_{i>\ell^{*}}(\sigma^{N}_{i})^{2}+O\left(\frac{\ell^{*}d_{2}\theta^{2}\sigma^{2}_{\epsilon}}{n}\right)+O(n^{-c_{0}})for some constant c0subscriptрқ‘җ0c_{0}. We next interpret each term in (2).

Terms вҲ‘i>в„“вҲ—(ПғiN)2+OвҖӢ(в„“вҲ—вҖӢd2вҖӢОё2вҖӢПғПө2n)subscriptрқ‘–superscriptв„“superscriptsubscriptsuperscriptрқңҺрқ‘Ғрқ‘–2рқ‘Ӯsuperscriptв„“subscriptрқ‘‘2superscriptрқңғ2subscriptsuperscriptрқңҺ2italic-Пөрқ‘ӣ\sum_{i>\ell^{*}}(\sigma^{N}_{i})^{2}+O\left(\frac{\ell^{*}d_{2}\theta^{2}\sigma^{2}_{\epsilon}}{n}\right)  are typical for solving a matrix denoising problem N^+T+в„°(вүҲNT+в„°)annotatedsubscriptsuperscript^рқ‘ҒTв„°absentsuperscriptрқ‘ҒTв„°\hat{N}^{\mathrm{T}}_{+}+\mathcal{E}(\approx N^{\mathrm{T}}+\mathcal{E}): we can extract signals associated with в„“вҲ—superscriptв„“\ell^{*} leading singular vectors of Nрқ‘ҒN, so вҲ‘i>в„“вҲ—(ПғiN)2subscriptрқ‘–superscriptв„“superscriptsubscriptsuperscriptрқңҺрқ‘Ғрқ‘–2\sum_{i>\ell^{*}}(\sigma^{N}_{i})^{2} starts at i>в„“вҲ—рқ‘–superscriptв„“i>\ell^{*}. For each direction we extract, we need to pay a noise term of orderОё2вҖӢПғПө2вҖӢd2nsuperscriptрқңғ2subscriptsuperscriptрқңҺ2italic-Пөsubscriptрқ‘‘2рқ‘ӣ\theta^{2}\sigma^{2}_{\epsilon}\frac{d_{2}}{n}, leading to the term OвҖӢ(в„“вҲ—вҖӢd2вҖӢОё2вҖӢПғПө2n)рқ‘Ӯsuperscriptв„“subscriptрқ‘‘2superscriptрқңғ2subscriptsuperscriptрқңҺ2italic-Пөрқ‘ӣO\left(\frac{\ell^{*}d_{2}\theta^{2}\sigma^{2}_{\epsilon}}{n}\right).Terms OвҖӢ(ОҫОҙ3)+OвҖӢ(ОҙПүвҲ’14вҖӢ(Пү+1))рқ‘Ӯрқңүsuperscriptрқӣҝ3рқ‘Ӯsuperscriptрқӣҝрқң”14рқң”1O\left(\sqrt{\frac{\xi}{\delta^{3}}}\right)+O\left(\delta^{\frac{\omega-1}{4(\omega+1)}}\right) come from the estimations error of рқҗі^+subscript^рқҗі\hat{\mathbf{z}}_{+} produced from Prop.В 1, consisting of both estimation errors of CвҲ—superscriptрқҗ¶C^{*}вҖҷs leading eigenvectors and the error of cutting out a tail.We pay an exponent of 1414\frac{1}{4} on both terms (e.g., ОҙПүвҲ’1Пү+1superscriptрқӣҝрқң”1рқң”1\delta^{\frac{\omega-1}{\omega+1}} in Prop.В 1 becomes ОҙПүвҲ’14вҖӢ(Пү+1)superscriptрқӣҝрқң”14рқң”1\delta^{\frac{\omega-1}{4(\omega+1)}}) because we used Cauchy-Schwarz (CS) twice. One is used inrunning matrix denoising algorithm with inaccurate рқҗі+subscriptрқҗі\mathbf{z}_{+}; the other one is used to bound the impact of cutting a tail. It remains open whether two CS is can be circumvented.

Sec.В 4 explains how ThmВ 1 and the lower bound imply the algorithm is near-optimal. Sec.В 5 compares our result with existing ones under other parametrizations, e.g. rankвҖӢ(M)rankрқ‘Җ\mathrm{rank}(M).

We now analyze our algorithm. Our analysis consists of three steps. In step 1, we prove PropositionВ 1. In step 2, we relate рқҗҷTвҖӢрқҗҳsuperscriptрқҗҷTрқҗҳ\mathbf{Z}^{\mathrm{T}}\mathbf{Y} with the product produced by our estimate рқҗҷ^+TвҖӢрқҗҳsubscriptsuperscript^рқҗҷTрқҗҳ\hat{\mathbf{Z}}^{\mathrm{T}}_{+}\mathbf{Y}. In step 3, we prove TheoremВ 1.

This section proves PropositionВ 1.We shall first show that the algorithm always terminates. We have the following lemma.

We remark that LemmaВ 1 will also be able to show part (ii) of PropositionВ 1 (this will be explained below). This lemma also corresponds to the вҖңconnection between gap and tailвҖқ building block referred in SectionВ 3.1.

Define the function hвҖӢ(t)=вҲ‘iвүҘtc/iПү=c3+oвҖӢ(1)tПүвҲ’1в„Һрқ‘Ўsubscriptрқ‘–рқ‘Ўрқ‘җsuperscriptрқ‘–рқң”subscriptрқ‘җ3рқ‘ң1superscriptрқ‘Ўрқң”1h(t)=\sum_{i\geq t}c/i^{\omega}=\frac{c_{3}+o(1)}{t^{\omega-1}} (by EulerвҖ“Maclaurin formula), where oвҖӢ(1)рқ‘ң1o(1) is a function of tрқ‘Ўt

Next, let us definei1subscriptрқ‘–1\displaystyle i_{1}=minвҒЎ{iвҲ—:вҲ‘iвүӨiвҲ—О»iвүҘ1вҲ’hвҖӢ(в„“П„ПүвҲ’1)}вҲ’1absent:superscriptрқ‘–subscriptрқ‘–superscriptрқ‘–subscriptрқңҶрқ‘–1в„Һsuperscriptв„“рқңҸрқң”11\displaystyle=\min\left\{i^{*}:\sum_{i\leq i^{*}}\lambda_{i}\geq 1-h({\ell}^{\frac{\tau}{\omega-1}})\right\}-1i2subscriptрқ‘–2\displaystyle i_{2}=minвҒЎ{iвҲ—:вҲ‘iвүӨiвҲ—О»iвүҘ1вҲ’12Г—hвҖӢ(в„“П„ПүвҲ’1)}вҲ’1.absent:superscriptрқ‘–subscriptрқ‘–superscriptрқ‘–subscriptрқңҶрқ‘–112в„Һsuperscriptв„“рқңҸрқң”11\displaystyle=\min\left\{i^{*}:\sum_{i\leq i^{*}}\lambda_{i}\geq 1-\frac{1}{2}\times h({\ell}^{\frac{\tau}{\omega-1}})\right\}-1.

Roughly speaking, we want to identify an i1subscriptрқ‘–1i_{1} such that вҲ‘iвүӨi1О»isubscriptрқ‘–subscriptрқ‘–1subscriptрқңҶрқ‘–\sum_{i\leq i_{1}}\lambda_{i} is smaller than 1вҲ’hвҖӢ(в„“П„ПүвҲ’1)1в„Һsuperscriptв„“рқңҸрқң”11-h\left(\ell^{\frac{\tau}{\omega-1}}\right) but is as close to it as possible. We can interpret i2subscriptрқ‘–2i_{2} in a similar manner. i1,i2вүҘ1subscriptрқ‘–1subscriptрқ‘–21i_{1},i_{2}\geq 1 because of the assumption О»1<1subscriptрқңҶ11\lambda_{1}<1.

We can verify that i1<в„“П„ПүвҲ’1subscriptрқ‘–1superscriptв„“рқңҸрқң”1i_{1}<\ell^{\frac{\tau}{\omega-1}} because вҲ‘iвүӨв„“П„ПүвҲ’1О»iвүҘ1вҲ’hвҖӢ(в„“П„ПүвҲ’1)subscriptрқ‘–superscriptв„“рқңҸрқң”1subscriptрқңҶрқ‘–1в„Һsuperscriptв„“рқңҸрқң”1\sum_{i\leq\ell^{\frac{\tau}{\omega-1}}}\lambda_{i}\geq 1-h\left(\ell^{\frac{\tau}{\omega-1}}\right). It remains to prove part (i) of PropositionВ 1. It consists of three steps.

Step 1. Dimension-free Chernoff bound for matrices.  We first give a bound on вҖ–CвҲ—вҲ’CвҖ–2subscriptnormsuperscriptрқҗ¶рқҗ¶2\|C^{*}-C\|_{2}, which characterizes the tail probability by using the first and second moments of random vectors. This is the key device enabling us to meaningfully recover signals even when nвүӘd1much-less-thanрқ‘ӣsubscriptрқ‘‘1n\ll d_{1}.

The exponent 10 is chosen arbitrarily and is not optimized.

This completes the proof of PropositionВ 1.

The rest of this Section proves PropositionВ 2. Recall that рқҗҳ=рқҗҷвҖӢNT+Eрқҗҳрқҗҷsuperscriptрқ‘ҒTрқҗё\mathbf{Y}=\mathbf{Z}N^{\mathrm{T}}+E is the orthogonalized form of our problem. Let us split N=[N+,NвҲ’]рқ‘Ғsubscriptрқ‘Ғsubscriptрқ‘ҒN=[N_{+},N_{-}], where N+вҲҲрқҗ‘d2Г—k1subscriptрқ‘Ғsuperscriptрқҗ‘subscriptрқ‘‘2subscriptрқ‘ҳ1N_{+}\in\mathbf{R}^{d_{2}\times k_{1}} consists of the k1subscriptрқ‘ҳ1k_{1} leading columns of Nрқ‘ҒN andNвҲ’вҲҲрқҗ‘d2Г—(d1вҲ’k1)subscriptрқ‘Ғsuperscriptрқҗ‘subscriptрқ‘‘2subscriptрқ‘‘1subscriptрқ‘ҳ1N_{-}\in\mathbf{R}^{d_{2}\times(d_{1}-k_{1})} consists of the remaining columns. Similarly, let рқҗі=[рқҗі+,рқҗівҲ’]рқҗіsubscriptрқҗіsubscriptрқҗі\mathbf{z}=[\mathbf{z}_{+},\mathbf{z}_{-}], where рқҗі+вҲҲрқҗ‘nГ—k1subscriptрқҗіsuperscriptрқҗ‘рқ‘ӣsubscriptрқ‘ҳ1\mathbf{z}_{+}\in\mathbf{R}^{n\times k_{1}} and рқҗівҲ’вҲҲрқҗ‘nГ—(d1вҲ’k1)subscriptрқҗіsuperscriptрқҗ‘рқ‘ӣsubscriptрқ‘‘1subscriptрқ‘ҳ1\mathbf{z}_{-}\in\mathbf{R}^{n\times(d_{1}-k_{1})}. Let рқҗҷ=[рқҗҷ+,рқҗҷвҲ’]рқҗҷsubscriptрқҗҷsubscriptрқҗҷ\mathbf{Z}=[\mathbf{Z}_{+},\mathbf{Z}_{-}], where рқҗҷ+вҲҲрқҗ‘nГ—k1subscriptрқҗҷsuperscriptрқҗ‘рқ‘ӣsubscriptрқ‘ҳ1\mathbf{Z}_{+}\in\mathbf{R}^{n\times k_{1}} and рқҗҷвҲ’вҲҲрқҗ‘nГ—(d1вҲ’k1)subscriptрқҗҷsuperscriptрқҗ‘рқ‘ӣsubscriptрқ‘‘1subscriptрқ‘ҳ1\mathbf{Z}_{-}\in\mathbf{R}^{n\times(d_{1}-k_{1})}. We next analyze each term. We aim to find bounds in either spectral norm or Frobenius norm. In some cases, it suffices to use вҖ–в„°iвҖ–2вӢ…rankвҖӢ(в„°i)вӢ…subscriptnormsubscriptв„°рқ‘–2ranksubscriptв„°рқ‘–\|\mathcal{E}_{i}\|_{2}\cdot\mathrm{rank}(\mathcal{E}_{i}) to upper bound вҖ–в„°iвҖ–Fsubscriptnormsubscriptв„°рқ‘–рқҗ№\|\mathcal{E}_{i}\|_{F}. On the other hand, in the case of analyzing в„°5subscriptв„°5\mathcal{E}_{5}, we can get a tight Frobenius norm bound but we cannot get a non-trivial spectral bound.

From time to time, we will label the dimension of matrices in complex multiplication operations to enable readers to do sanity checks.

Bounding в„°3subscriptв„°3\mathcal{E}_{3}.   We have the following Lemma.

Let t=maxвҒЎ{10вҖӢlog2вҒЎnn,4вҖӢk1n}рқ‘Ў10superscript2рқ‘ӣрқ‘ӣ4subscriptрқ‘ҳ1рқ‘ӣt=\max\left\{\frac{10\log^{2}n}{\sqrt{n}},4\sqrt{\frac{k_{1}}{n}}\right\}. By LemmaВ 7, with high probability вҖ–1nвҖӢрқҗҷTвҖӢрқҗҷвҲ’IвҖ–вүӨtnorm1рқ‘ӣsuperscriptрқҗҷTрқҗҷрқҗјрқ‘Ў\|\frac{1}{n}\mathbf{Z}^{\mathrm{T}}\mathbf{Z}-I\|\leq t. This implies that the eigenvalues of рқҗҷTвҖӢрқҗҷsuperscriptрқҗҷTрқҗҷ\mathbf{Z}^{\mathrm{T}}\mathbf{Z} are all within the range nвҖӢ(1Вұt)рқ‘ӣplus-or-minus1рқ‘Ўn(1\pm t). Note that for 0<О·<1/30рқңӮ130<\eta<1/3, if ОҫвҲҲ[1вҲ’О·,1+О·]рқңү1рқңӮ1рқңӮ\xi\in[1-\eta,1+\eta], then ОҫвҲҲ[1вҲ’2вҖӢО·,1+2вҖӢО·]рқңү12рқңӮ12рқңӮ\sqrt{\xi}\in[1-2\eta,1+2\eta]. This implies that the singular values of рқҗҷрқҗҷ\mathbf{Z} are within the range nвҖӢ(1Вұ2вҖӢt)рқ‘ӣplus-or-minus12рқ‘Ў\sqrt{n}(1\pm 2t).

Let ОЈZ/n=I+О”ZsuperscriptОЈрқ‘Қрқ‘ӣрқҗјsuperscriptО”рқ‘Қ\Sigma^{Z}/\sqrt{n}=I+\Delta^{Z}, where вҖ–О”ZвҖ–вүӨ2вҖӢtnormsuperscriptО”рқ‘Қ2рқ‘Ў\|\Delta^{Z}\|\leq 2t.We have1nвҖӢрқҗҷTвҖӢE1рқ‘ӣsuperscriptрқҗҷTрқҗё\displaystyle\frac{1}{n}\mathbf{Z}^{\mathrm{T}}E=VZвҖӢ(ОЈZn)вҖӢ(UZ)TвҖӢEn=VZвҖӢ(I+О”Z)вҖӢ(UZ)TвҖӢEnabsentsuperscriptрқ‘үрқ‘ҚsuperscriptОЈрқ‘Қрқ‘ӣsuperscriptsuperscriptрқ‘Ҳрқ‘ҚTрқҗёрқ‘ӣsuperscriptрқ‘үрқ‘ҚрқҗјsuperscriptО”рқ‘Қsuperscriptsuperscriptрқ‘Ҳрқ‘ҚTрқҗёрқ‘ӣ\displaystyle=V^{Z}\left(\frac{\Sigma^{Z}}{\sqrt{n}}\right)(U^{Z})^{\mathrm{T}}\frac{E}{\sqrt{n}}=V^{Z}(I+\Delta^{Z})(U^{Z})^{\mathrm{T}}\frac{E}{\sqrt{n}}=VZвҸҹk1Г—k1вҖӢ(UZ)TвҸҹk1Г—nвҖӢEnвҸҹnГ—d2+VZвҖӢО”ZвҖӢ(UZ)TвҖӢEn.absentsubscriptвҸҹsuperscriptрқ‘үрқ‘Қsubscriptрқ‘ҳ1subscriptрқ‘ҳ1subscriptвҸҹsuperscriptsuperscriptрқ‘Ҳрқ‘ҚTsubscriptрқ‘ҳ1рқ‘ӣsubscriptвҸҹрқҗёрқ‘ӣрқ‘ӣsubscriptрқ‘‘2superscriptрқ‘үрқ‘ҚsuperscriptО”рқ‘Қsuperscriptsuperscriptрқ‘Ҳрқ‘ҚTрқҗёрқ‘ӣ\displaystyle=\underbrace{V^{Z}}_{k_{1}\times k_{1}}\underbrace{(U^{Z})^{\mathrm{T}}}_{k_{1}\times n}\underbrace{\frac{E}{\sqrt{n}}}_{n\times d_{2}}+V^{Z}\Delta^{Z}(U^{Z})^{\mathrm{T}}\frac{E}{\sqrt{n}}.(21)Using the fact that the columns of UZsuperscriptрқ‘Ҳрқ‘ҚU^{Z} are orthonormal vectors, VZsuperscriptрқ‘үрқ‘ҚV^{Z} is a unitary matrix, and k1вүӨd2subscriptрқ‘ҳ1subscriptрқ‘‘2k_{1}\leq d_{2}, we see that VZвҖӢ(UZ)TвҖӢE/nsuperscriptрқ‘үрқ‘Қsuperscriptsuperscriptрқ‘Ҳрқ‘ҚTрқҗёрқ‘ӣV^{Z}(U^{Z})^{\mathrm{T}}E/\sqrt{n} is a matrix with i.i.d. To understand the reason we perform such grouping, we can imagine making a decision for an (overly) simplified problem for each direction in the basis: consider a univariate estimation problem y=Ој+Пөрқ‘ҰрқңҮitalic-Пөy=\mu+\epsilon with ОјрқңҮ\mu being the signal, ПөвҲјNвҖӢ(0,Пғ2)similar-toitalic-Пөрқ‘Ғ0superscriptрқңҺ2\epsilon\sim N(0,\sigma^{2}) being the noise, and yрқ‘Ұy being the observation. Let us consider the case we observe only one sample. Now when yвү«Пғmuch-greater-thanрқ‘ҰрқңҺy\gg\sigma, we can use yрқ‘Ұy as the estimator and IвҖӢEвҖӢ[(yвҲ’Ој)2]=Пғ2IEdelimited-[]superscriptрқ‘ҰрқңҮ2superscriptрқңҺ2\mathrm{I\!E}[(y-\mu)^{2}]=\sigma^{2}. This high signal-to-noise setting corresponds to the vectors in Group 1.

When yвүҲ3вҖӢПғрқ‘Ұ3рқңҺy\approx 3\sigma, we have Ој2=IвҖӢEвҖӢ[(yвҲ’Пө)2]вүҲ(3вҲ’1)2вҖӢПғ2=4вҖӢПғ2superscriptрқңҮ2IEdelimited-[]superscriptрқ‘Ұitalic-Пө2superscript312superscriptрқңҺ24superscriptрқңҺ2\mu^{2}=\mathrm{I\!E}[(y-\epsilon)^{2}]\approx(3-1)^{2}\sigma^{2}=4\sigma^{2}. On the other hand, IвҖӢEвҖӢ[(yвҲ’Ој)2]=Пғ2IEdelimited-[]superscriptрқ‘ҰрқңҮ2superscriptрқңҺ2\mathrm{I\!E}[(y-\mu)^{2}]=\sigma^{2}. This means if we use yрқ‘Ұy as the estimator, the forecast is at least better than trivial. The median signal-to-noise setting corresponds to the vectors in group 2.

When yвүӘПғmuch-less-thanрқ‘ҰрқңҺy\ll\sigma, we can simply use y^=0^рқ‘Ұ0\hat{y}=0 as the estimator. This low signal-to-noise setting corresponds to vectors in group 3.

In other words, we expect: (i) In term 1, signals along each direction of vectors in group 1 can be extracted. Each direction also pays a Пғ2superscriptрқңҺ2\sigma^{2} term, which in our setting corresponds to ОёвҖӢПғПөвҖӢd2nрқңғsubscriptрқңҺitalic-Пөsubscriptрқ‘‘2рқ‘ӣ\theta\sigma_{\epsilon}\sqrt{\frac{d_{2}}{n}}. Therefore, the MSE can be bounded by OвҖӢ(в„“вҖӢОё2вҖӢПғПө2вҖӢd2/n)рқ‘Ӯв„“superscriptрқңғ2subscriptsuperscriptрқңҺ2italic-Пөsubscriptрқ‘‘2рқ‘ӣO(\ell\theta^{2}\sigma^{2}_{\epsilon}d_{2}/n). (ii) In terms 2 and 3, we do at least (almost) as well as the вҖңtrivial forecastвҖқ (рқҗІ^=0^рқҗІ0\hat{\mathbf{y}}=0). There is also an error produced by the estimator error from рқҗі^+subscript^рқҗі\hat{\mathbf{z}}_{+}, and the tail error produced from cutting out features in \procвҖӢSвҖӢtвҖӢeвҖӢpвҲ’1вҲ’PвҖӢCвҖӢAвҲ’X\procрқ‘Ҷрқ‘Ўрқ‘’рқ‘қ1рқ‘ғрқҗ¶рқҗҙрқ‘Ӣ\proc{Step-1-PCA-X} in Fig.В 1.

We haveОҰ1+ОҰ2+2вҖӢОҰ1вҖӢОҰ2subscriptОҰ1subscriptОҰ22subscriptОҰ1subscriptОҰ2\displaystyle\Phi_{1}+\Phi_{2}+2\sqrt{\Phi_{1}\Phi_{2}}=ОҰ1вҖӢ(1+2вҖӢОҰ2ОҰ1)+ОҰ2absentsubscriptОҰ112subscriptОҰ2subscriptОҰ1subscriptОҰ2\displaystyle=\Phi_{1}(1+2\sqrt{\frac{\Phi_{2}}{\Phi_{1}}})+\Phi_{2}=[вҖ–NвҖ–F2вҲ’вҲ‘iвүӨв„“вҲ—(ПғiN)2+OвҖӢ(в„“вҲ—вҖӢd2вҖӢОё2вҖӢПғПө2n)+OвҖӢ(Оҫ/Оҙ3)+OвҖӢ(ОҙПүвҲ’1Пү+1)]absentdelimited-[]subscriptsuperscriptnormрқ‘Ғ2рқҗ№subscriptрқ‘–superscriptв„“superscriptsubscriptsuperscriptрқңҺрқ‘Ғрқ‘–2рқ‘Ӯsuperscriptв„“subscriptрқ‘‘2superscriptрқңғ2subscriptsuperscriptрқңҺ2italic-Пөрқ‘ӣрқ‘Ӯрқңүsuperscriptрқӣҝ3рқ‘Ӯsuperscriptрқӣҝрқң”1рқң”1\displaystyle=\left[\|N\|^{2}_{F}-\sum_{i\leq\ell^{*}}(\sigma^{N}_{i})^{2}+O\left(\frac{\ell^{*}d_{2}\theta^{2}\sigma^{2}_{\epsilon}}{n}\right)+O(\xi/\delta^{3})+O\left(\sqrt{\delta^{\frac{\omega-1}{\omega+1}}}\right)\right]Г—{1+minвҒЎ{ОҫОҙ3+(ОҙПүвҲ’1Пү+1)14}}+OвҖӢ(Оҫ2Оҙ6)+OвҖӢ(ОҙПүвҲ’1Пү+1)absent1рқңүsuperscriptрқӣҝ3superscriptsuperscriptрқӣҝрқң”1рқң”114рқ‘Ӯsuperscriptрқңү2superscriptрқӣҝ6рқ‘Ӯsuperscriptрқӣҝрқң”1рқң”1\displaystyle\quad\quad\times\left\{1+\min\left\{\sqrt{\frac{\xi}{\delta^{3}}}+\left(\delta^{\frac{\omega-1}{\omega+1}}\right)^{\frac{1}{4}}\right\}\right\}+O\left(\frac{\xi^{2}}{\delta^{6}}\right)+O\left(\delta^{\frac{\omega-1}{\omega+1}}\right)вүӨвҖ–NвҖ–F2вҲ’вҲ‘iвүӨв„“вҲ—(ПғiN)2+OвҖӢ(в„“вҲ—вҖӢd2вҖӢОё2вҖӢПғПө2n)+OвҖӢ(ОҫОҙ3)+OвҖӢ(ОҙПүвҲ’14вҖӢ(Пү+1)).absentsubscriptsuperscriptnormрқ‘Ғ2рқҗ№subscriptрқ‘–superscriptв„“subscriptsuperscriptsubscriptsuperscriptрқңҺрқ‘Ғрқ‘–2рқ‘Ӯsubscriptsuperscriptв„“subscriptрқ‘‘2superscriptрқңғ2subscriptsuperscriptрқңҺ2italic-Пөрқ‘ӣрқ‘Ӯsubscriptрқңүsuperscriptрқӣҝ3рқ‘Ӯsubscriptsuperscriptрқӣҝрқң”14рқң”1\displaystyle\leq{\|N\|^{2}_{F}-\sum_{i\leq\ell^{*}}(\sigma^{N}_{i})^{2}}_{\mbox{}}+{O\left(\frac{\ell^{*}d_{2}\theta^{2}\sigma^{2}_{\epsilon}}{n}\right)}_{\mbox{}}+{O\left(\sqrt{\frac{\xi}{\delta^{3}}}\right)}_{\mbox{}}+{O\left(\delta^{\frac{\omega-1}{4(\omega+1)}}\right)}_{\mbox{}}.(31)

This completes the proof of TheoremВ 1.

Our algorithm accurately estimates the singular vectors of Nрқ‘ҒN that correspondto singular values above the threshold П„=ОёвҖӢПғПөвҖӢd2nрқңҸрқңғsubscriptрқңҺitalic-Пөsubscriptрқ‘‘2рқ‘ӣ\tau=\theta\sigma_{\epsilon}{\sqrt{\frac{d_{2}}{n}}}. However, it may well happen that most of the spectral вҖҳmassвҖҷ of Nрқ‘ҒN lies only slightly below this threshold П„рқңҸ\tau. In this section, we establish that no algorithm can do better than us, in a bi-criteria sense, i.e. we show that any algorithm that has a slightly smaller sample than ours can only minimally outperform ours in terms of MSE.

We establish вҖҳinstance dependentвҖҷ lower bounds: When there is more вҖҳspectralmassвҖҷ below the threshold, the performance of our algorithm will be worse, andwe will need to establish that no algorithm can do much better. This departsfrom the standard minimax framework, in which one examines the entire parameterspace of Nрқ‘ҒN, e.g. all rank rрқ‘ҹr matrices, and produces a large set ofstatistically indistinguishable вҖҳbadвҖҷinstancesВ tsybakov2008introduction . These lower bounds are not sensitiveto instance-specific quantities such as the spectrum of Nрқ‘ҒN, and in particular, if priorknowledge suggests that the unknown parameter Nрқ‘ҒN is far from these bad instances,the minimax lower bound cannot be applied.

We introduce the notion of local minimax. We partition the space intoparts so that similar matrices are together.Similar matrices are those Nрқ‘ҒN that have the same singular values and rightsingular vectors; we establish strong lower bounds even against algorithms thatknow the singular values and right singular vectors of Nрқ‘ҒN. An equivalent viewis to assume that the algorithm has oracle access to CвҲ—superscriptрқҗ¶C^{*}, Mрқ‘ҖMвҖҷs singularvalues, and Mрқ‘ҖMвҖҷs right singular vectors. This algorithm can solvethe orthogonalized form as Nрқ‘ҒNвҖҷs singular values and right singular vectors caneasily be deduced. Thus, the only reason why the algorithm needs data is tolearn the left singular vectors of Nрқ‘ҒN. The lower bound we establish is the minimaxbound for this вҖҳunfairвҖҷ comparison, where the competing algorithm is given moreinformation. In fact, this can be reduced further, i.e., even ifthe algorithm вҖҳknowsвҖҷ that the left singular vectors of Nрқ‘ҒN are sparse,identifying the locations of the non-zero entries is the key difficulty thatleads to the lower bound.

It is worth interpreting (33) in some detail. For anytwo (M,рқҗұ)рқ‘Җрқҗұ(M,\mathbf{x}), (MвҖІ,рқҗұвҖІ)superscriptрқ‘ҖвҖІsuperscriptрқҗұвҖІ(M^{\prime},\mathbf{x}^{\prime}) in в„ӣвҖӢ(M,рқҗұ)в„ӣрқ‘Җрқҗұ\mathcal{R}(M,\mathbf{x}), the algorithm has the sameвҖҳprior knowledgeвҖҷ, so it can only distinguish between the twoinstances by using the observed data, in particular M^^рқ‘Җ\hat{M} is afunction only of рқҗ—рқҗ—\mathbf{X} and рқҗҳрқҗҳ\mathbf{Y}, and we denote it as M^вҖӢ(рқҗ—,рқҗҳ)^рқ‘Җрқҗ—рқҗҳ\hat{M}(\mathbf{X},\mathbf{Y}) toemphasize this. Thus, we can evaluate the performance of M^^рқ‘Җ\hat{M} by looking atthe worst possible (MвҖІ,рқҗұвҖІ)superscriptрқ‘ҖвҖІsuperscriptрқҗұвҖІ(M^{\prime},\mathbf{x}^{\prime}) and considering the MSE IвҖӢEвҖӢвҖ–M^вҖӢ(рқҗ—,рқҗҳ)вҖӢрқҗұвҖІвҲ’MвҖІвҖӢрқҗұвҖІвҖ–2IEsuperscriptnorm^рқ‘Җрқҗ—рқҗҳsuperscriptрқҗұвҖІsuperscriptрқ‘ҖвҖІsuperscriptрқҗұвҖІ2\mathrm{I\!E}\|\hat{M}(\mathbf{X},\mathbf{Y})\mathbf{x}^{\prime}-M^{\prime}\mathbf{x}^{\prime}\|^{2}.

PropositionВ 3 gives the lower bound on the MSE inexpectation; it can be turned into a high probability result with suitablemodifications. The proof of the lower bound uses a similarвҖҳtrickвҖҷ to the one used in the analysis of the upper bound analysis to cut the tail. This results in an additional termOвҖӢ(ПҒ12вҲ’Оҫd2ПүвҲ’1)рқ‘ӮsuperscriptрқңҢ12рқңүsuperscriptsubscriptрқ‘‘2рқң”1O\Bigl{(}\frac{\rho^{\frac{1}{2}-\xi}}{d_{2}^{\omega-1}}\Bigr{)}which is generally smaller than thenвҲ’c0superscriptрқ‘ӣsubscriptрқ‘җ0n^{-c_{0}} tail term in TheoremВ 1 anddoes not dominate the gap.

Gap requirement and bi-criteria approximation algorithms. Let П„=ПғПөвҖӢd2nрқңҸsubscriptрқңҺitalic-Пөsubscriptрқ‘‘2рқ‘ӣ\tau=\sigma_{\epsilon}\sqrt{\frac{d_{2}}{n}}.TheoremВ 1 asserts that any signal above the thresholdОёвҖӢП„рқңғрқңҸ\theta\tau can be detected, i.e., the MSE is at most вҲ‘ПғiN>ОёвҖӢП„Пғi2вҖӢ(N)subscriptsubscriptsuperscriptрқңҺрқ‘Ғрқ‘–рқңғрқңҸsubscriptsuperscriptрқңҺ2рқ‘–рқ‘Ғ\sum_{\sigma^{N}_{i}>\theta\tau}\sigma^{2}_{i}(N) (plus inevitable noise), whereasPropositionВ 3 asserts that any signal below the thresholdПҒвҖӢП„рқңҢрқңҸ\rho\tau cannot be detected, i.e., the MSE is approximately at leastвҲ‘ПғiNвүҘПҒвҖӢП„(1вҲ’polyвҖӢ(ПҒ))вҖӢПғi2вҖӢ(N)subscriptsubscriptsuperscriptрқңҺрқ‘Ғрқ‘–рқңҢрқңҸ1polyрқңҢsubscriptsuperscriptрқңҺ2рқ‘–рқ‘Ғ\sum_{\sigma^{N}_{i}\geq\rho\tau}(1-\mathrm{poly}(\rho))\sigma^{2}_{i}(N). Thereis a вҖҳgapвҖҷ between ОёвҖӢП„рқңғрқңҸ\theta\tau and ПҒвҖӢП„рқңҢрқңҸ\rho\tau, as Оё>1рқңғ1\theta>1 and ПҒ<1рқңҢ1\rho<1. See Fig.В 3(a). This kind of gap is inevitable because both bounds are вҖҳhigh probabilityвҖҷstatements. This gap phenomenon appears naturally when the sample size is smallas can be illustrated by this simple example. Consider the problem ofestimating ОјрқңҮ\mu when we see one sample from NвҖӢ(Ој,Пғ2)рқ‘ҒрқңҮsuperscriptрқңҺ2N(\mu,\sigma^{2}). Roughlyspeaking, when Ојвү«Пғmuch-greater-thanрқңҮрқңҺ\mu\gg\sigma, the estimation is feasible, and whereas ОјвүӘПғmuch-less-thanрқңҮрқңҺ\mu\ll\sigma, the estimation is impossible. For the region ОјвүҲПғрқңҮрқңҺ\mu\approx\sigma,algorithms fail with constant probability and we cannot prove a highprobability lower bound either.

While many of the signals can вҖҳhideвҖҷ in the gap, the inability to detect signals in the gap is a transient phenomenon. When the number of samples nрқ‘ӣn ismodestly increased, our detection threshold П„=ОёвҖӢПғПөвҖӢd2nрқңҸрқңғsubscriptрқңҺitalic-Пөsubscriptрқ‘‘2рқ‘ӣ\tau=\theta\sigma_{\epsilon}\sqrt{\frac{d_{2}}{n}} shrinks, and this hidden signal can befully recovered. This observation naturally leads to a notion of bi-criteriaoptimization that frequently arises in approximation algorithms.

The error term ОІрқӣҪ\beta consists of ПҒ12вҲ’ПөвҖӢвҖ–MвҖӢрқҗұвҖ–22superscriptрқңҢ12italic-Пөsubscriptsuperscriptnormрқ‘Җрқҗұ22\rho^{\frac{1}{2}-\epsilon}\|M\mathbf{x}\|^{2}_{2} thatis directly characterized by the signal strength and an additive termOвҖӢ(nвҲ’c0)=oвҖӢ(1)рқ‘Ӯsuperscriptрқ‘ӣsubscriptрқ‘җ0рқ‘ң1O(n^{-c_{0}})=o(1). Assuming that вҖ–MвҖӢрқҗұвҖ–=О©вҖӢ(1)normрқ‘ҖрқҗұО©1\|M\mathbf{x}\|=\Omega(1), i.e., the signalis not too weak, the term ОІрқӣҪ\beta becomes a single multiplicativeboundOвҖӢ(ПҒ12вҲ’Оҫ+nвҲ’c0)вҖӢвҖ–MвҖӢрқҗұвҖ–22рқ‘ӮsuperscriptрқңҢ12рқңүsuperscriptрқ‘ӣsubscriptрқ‘җ0subscriptsuperscriptnormрқ‘Җрқҗұ22O(\rho^{\frac{1}{2}-\xi}+n^{-c_{0}})\|M\mathbf{x}\|^{2}_{2}.This gives an easily interpretable result. For example, when our data size isnвҖӢlogвҒЎnрқ‘ӣрқ‘ӣn\log n, the performance gap between our algorithm and any algorithmthat uses nрқ‘ӣn samples is at most oвҖӢ(вҖ–MвҖӢрқҗұвҖ–22)рқ‘ңsubscriptsuperscriptnormрқ‘Җрқҗұ22o(\|M\mathbf{x}\|^{2}_{2}). The improvement issignificant when other baselines deliver MSE in the additive form that could belarger than вҖ–MвҖӢрқҗұвҖ–22subscriptsuperscriptnormрқ‘Җрқҗұ22\|M\mathbf{x}\|^{2}_{2} in the regime nвүӨd1рқ‘ӣsubscriptрқ‘‘1n\leq d_{1}.

Preview of techniques.  Let N=UNвҖӢОЈNвҖӢ(VN)Tрқ‘Ғsuperscriptрқ‘Ҳрқ‘ҒsuperscriptОЈрқ‘Ғsuperscriptsuperscriptрқ‘үрқ‘ҒTN=U^{N}\Sigma^{N}(V^{N})^{\mathrm{T}} be the instance (in orthogonalized form). Our goal is to construct a collection рқ’©={N1,вҖҰ,NK}рқ’©subscriptрқ‘Ғ1вҖҰsubscriptрқ‘Ғрқҗҫ\mathcal{N}=\{N_{1},\dots,N_{K}\} of KрқҗҫK matrices so that (i) For any NiвҲҲрқ’©subscriptрқ‘Ғрқ‘–рқ’©N_{i}\in\mathcal{N}, ОЈNi=ОЈNsuperscriptОЈsubscriptрқ‘Ғрқ‘–superscriptОЈрқ‘Ғ\Sigma^{N_{i}}=\Sigma^{N} and VNi=VNsuperscriptрқ‘үsubscriptрқ‘Ғрқ‘–superscriptрқ‘үрқ‘ҒV^{N_{i}}=V^{N}. (ii) For any two Ni,NjвҲҲрқ’©subscriptрқ‘Ғрқ‘–subscriptрқ‘Ғрқ‘—рқ’©N_{i},N_{j}\in\mathcal{N}, вҖ–NвҲ’NвҖІвҖ–Fsubscriptnormрқ‘Ғsuperscriptрқ‘ҒвҖІрқҗ№\|N-N^{\prime}\|_{F} is large, and (iii) K=expвҒЎ(О©вҖӢ(polyвҖӢ(ПҒ)вҖӢd2))рқҗҫО©polyрқңҢsuperscriptрқ‘‘2K=\exp(\Omega(\mathrm{poly}(\rho)d^{2})) (cf.В (tsybakov2008introduction, , Chap. 2)).

Condition (i) ensures that it suffices to construct unitary matricesUNisuperscriptрқ‘Ҳsubscriptрқ‘Ғрқ‘–U^{N_{i}}вҖҷs for рқ’©рқ’©\mathcal{N}, and that the resulting instances will be in the sameequivalence class. Conditions (ii) and (iii) resemble standard construction ofcodes in information theory: we need a large вҖҳcode rateвҖҷ, corresponding torequiring a large KрқҗҫK as well as large distances between codewords,corresponding to requiring that вҖ–UiвҲ’UjвҖ–Fsubscriptnormsubscriptрқ‘Ҳрқ‘–subscriptрқ‘Ҳрқ‘—рқҗ№\|U_{i}-U_{j}\|_{F} be large. Standard approachesfor constructing such collections run into difficulties. Getting a sufficientlytight concentration bound on the distance between two random unitary matricesis difficult as the matrix entries, by necessity, are correlated.On the other hand, starting with a large collection of random unit vectors andusing its Cartesian product to build matrices does not necessarily yieldunitary matrices.

We design a two-stage approach to decouple condition (iii) from (i) and (ii) by only generating sparse matrices UNisuperscriptрқ‘Ҳsubscriptрқ‘Ғрқ‘–U^{N_{i}}. See Fig.В 3(b)-(d). In the first stage (Steps 1 & 2 in Fig.В 3(b)-(c)), we only specify thenon-zero positions (sparsity pattern) in each UNisuperscriptрқ‘Ҳsubscriptрқ‘Ғрқ‘–U^{N_{i}}. It suffices toguarantee that the sparsity patterns of the matrices UNisuperscriptрқ‘Ҳsubscriptрқ‘Ғрқ‘–U^{N_{i}} and UNjsuperscriptрқ‘Ҳsubscriptрқ‘Ғрқ‘—U^{N_{j}}have little overlap. The existence of such objects can easily be proved usingthe probabilistic method. Thus, in the first stage, we can build up a largenumber of sparsity patterns. In the second stage (Step 3 in Fig.В 3(d)), we carefully fill in valuesin the non-zero positions for each UNisuperscriptрқ‘Ҳsubscriptрқ‘Ғрқ‘–U^{N_{i}}. When the number of non-zeroentries is not too small, satisfying the unitary constraint is feasible. As theoverlap of sparsity patterns of any two matrices is small, we can argue thedistance between them is large. By carefully trading off the number of non-zeropositions and the portion of overlap, we can simultaneously satisfy all threeconditions.

This section describes the roadmap for executing the above idea.

Normalized form.  Recall that d2вүӨd1subscriptрқ‘‘2subscriptрқ‘‘1d_{2}\leq d_{1}, we haveMвҖӢрқҗұ=UMвҸҹd2Г—d2вҖӢОЈMвҸҹd2Г—d2вҖӢ(VM)TвҸҹd2Г—d1вҖӢVвҲ—вҸҹd1Г—d1вҖӢ(ОӣвҲ—)12вҸҹd1Г—d1вҖӢрқҗівҸҹd1Г—1рқ‘ҖрқҗұsubscriptвҸҹsuperscriptрқ‘Ҳрқ‘Җsubscriptрқ‘‘2subscriptрқ‘‘2subscriptвҸҹsuperscriptОЈрқ‘Җsubscriptрқ‘‘2subscriptрқ‘‘2subscriptвҸҹsuperscriptsuperscriptрқ‘үрқ‘ҖTsubscriptрқ‘‘2subscriptрқ‘‘1subscriptвҸҹsuperscriptрқ‘үsubscriptрқ‘‘1subscriptрқ‘‘1subscriptвҸҹsuperscriptsuperscriptОӣ12subscriptрқ‘‘1subscriptрқ‘‘1subscriptвҸҹрқҗіsubscriptрқ‘‘11M\mathbf{x}=\underbrace{U^{M}}_{d_{2}\times d_{2}}\underbrace{\Sigma^{M}}_{d_{2}\times d_{2}}\underbrace{(V^{M})^{\mathrm{T}}}_{d_{2}\times d_{1}}\underbrace{V^{*}}_{d_{1}\times d_{1}}\underbrace{(\Lambda^{*})^{\frac{1}{2}}}_{d_{1}\times d_{1}}\underbrace{\mathbf{z}}_{d_{1}\times 1}(34)

We may perform an SVD on ОЈMвҖӢ(VM)TвҖӢVвҲ—вҖӢ(ОӣвҲ—)12=AвҸҹd2Г—d2вҖӢLвҖ вҸҹd2Г—d2вҖӢBTвҸҹd2Г—d1superscriptОЈрқ‘Җsuperscriptsuperscriptрқ‘үрқ‘ҖTsuperscriptрқ‘үsuperscriptsuperscriptОӣ12subscriptвҸҹрқҗҙsubscriptрқ‘‘2subscriptрқ‘‘2subscriptвҸҹsuperscriptрқҗҝвҖ subscriptрқ‘‘2subscriptрқ‘‘2subscriptвҸҹsuperscriptрқҗөTsubscriptрқ‘‘2subscriptрқ‘‘1\Sigma^{M}(V^{M})^{\mathrm{T}}V^{*}(\Lambda^{*})^{\frac{1}{2}}=\underbrace{A}_{d_{2}\times d_{2}}\underbrace{L^{\dagger}}_{d_{2}\times d_{2}}\underbrace{B^{\mathrm{T}}}_{d_{2}\times d_{1}}. We may also set рқҗівҖ =BTвҖӢрқҗіsuperscriptрқҗівҖ superscriptрқҗөTрқҗі\mathbf{z}^{\dagger}=B^{\mathrm{T}}\mathbf{z}, which is a standard multi-variate Gaussian in рқҗ‘d2superscriptрқҗ‘subscriptрқ‘‘2\mathbf{R}^{d_{2}}. Then we haveMвҖӢрқҗұ=UMвҖӢAвҖӢLвҖ вҖӢBTвҖӢрқҗі=(UMвҖӢA)вҖӢLвҖ вҖӢрқҗівҖ .рқ‘Җрқҗұsuperscriptрқ‘Ҳрқ‘ҖрқҗҙsuperscriptрқҗҝвҖ superscriptрқҗөTрқҗіsuperscriptрқ‘Ҳрқ‘ҖрқҗҙsuperscriptрқҗҝвҖ superscriptрқҗівҖ M\mathbf{x}=U^{M}AL^{\dagger}B^{\mathrm{T}}\mathbf{z}=(U^{M}A)L^{\dagger}\mathbf{z}^{\dagger}.(35)Let NвҖ =(UMвҖӢA)вҖӢLвҖ superscriptрқ‘ҒвҖ superscriptрқ‘Ҳрқ‘ҖрқҗҙsuperscriptрқҗҝвҖ N^{\dagger}=(U^{M}A)L^{\dagger}. The SVD of NвҖ superscriptрқ‘ҒвҖ N^{\dagger} is exactly (UM)вҖӢAвҖӢLвҖ вҖӢId2Г—d2superscriptрқ‘Ҳрқ‘ҖрқҗҙsuperscriptрқҗҝвҖ subscriptрқҗјsubscriptрқ‘‘2subscriptрқ‘‘2(U^{M})AL^{\dagger}I_{d_{2}\times d_{2}} because UMвҖӢAsuperscriptрқ‘Ҳрқ‘ҖрқҗҙU^{M}A is unitary.The normalized form of our problem isрқҗІ=NвҖ вҖӢрқҗівҖ +Пө.рқҗІsuperscriptрқ‘ҒвҖ superscriptрқҗівҖ italic-Пө\mathbf{y}=N^{\dagger}\mathbf{z}^{\dagger}+\epsilon.(36)

Recall our local minimax has an oracle access interpretation. An algorithm with the oracle can reduce a problem into the normalized form on its own, and the algorithm knows LвҖ superscriptрқҗҝвҖ L^{\dagger}. But the oracle still does not have any information on NвҖ superscriptрқ‘ҒвҖ N^{\dagger}вҖҷs left singular vectors because being able to manipulate UMsuperscriptрқ‘Ҳрқ‘ҖU^{M} is the same as being able to manipulate UMвҖӢAsuperscriptрқ‘Ҳрқ‘ҖрқҗҙU^{M}A. Therefore, we can analyze the lower bound in normalized form, with the assumption that the SVD of NвҖ =UвҖ вҖӢLвҖ вҖӢId2Г—d2superscriptрқ‘ҒвҖ superscriptрқ‘ҲвҖ superscriptрқҗҝвҖ subscriptрқҗјsubscriptрқ‘‘2subscriptрқ‘‘2N^{\dagger}=U^{\dagger}L^{\dagger}I_{d_{2}\times d_{2}}, in which LвҖ superscriptрқҗҝвҖ L^{\dagger} is known to the algorithm. We shall also let ПғiвҖ =Li,iвҖ =ПғiNвҖ subscriptsuperscriptрқңҺвҖ рқ‘–subscriptsuperscriptрқҗҝвҖ рқ‘–рқ‘–subscriptsuperscriptрқңҺsuperscriptрқ‘ҒвҖ рқ‘–\sigma^{\dagger}_{i}=L^{\dagger}_{i,i}=\sigma^{N^{\dagger}}_{i}. Because NвҖ superscriptрқ‘ҒвҖ N^{\dagger} is square, we let d=d2рқ‘‘subscriptрқ‘‘2d=d_{2} in the analysis below.

We make two remarks in comparison to the orthogonalized form рқҗІ=NвҖӢрқҗі+ПөрқҗІрқ‘Ғрқҗіitalic-Пө\mathbf{y}=N\mathbf{z}+\epsilon. (i) рқҗівҖ вҲҲрқҗ‘d2superscriptрқҗівҖ superscriptрқҗ‘subscriptрқ‘‘2\mathbf{z}^{\dagger}\in\mathbf{R}^{d_{2}}, whereas рқҗівҲҲрқҗ‘d1рқҗіsuperscriptрқҗ‘subscriptрқ‘‘1\mathbf{z}\in\mathbf{R}^{d_{1}}. рқҗівҖ superscriptрқҗівҖ \mathbf{z}^{\dagger}вҖҷs dimension is smaller because the knowledge of ОЈMsuperscriptОЈрқ‘Җ\Sigma^{M} and VMsuperscriptрқ‘үрқ‘ҖV^{M} enable us to remove the directions from рқҗұрқҗұ\mathbf{x} that are orthogonal to Mрқ‘ҖMвҖҷs row space. (ii) ПғiN=ПғiNвҖ subscriptsuperscriptрқңҺрқ‘Ғрқ‘–subscriptsuperscriptрқңҺsuperscriptрқ‘ҒвҖ рқ‘–\sigma^{N}_{i}=\sigma^{N^{\dagger}}_{i} for iвүӨd2рқ‘–subscriptрқ‘‘2i\leq d_{2}.

We rely on the following theorem (Chapter 2 inВ tsybakov2008introduction ) to construct the lower bound.

Because LвҖ superscriptрқҗҝвҖ L^{\dagger} is fixed, this problem boils down to finding a collection рқ•ҢвҖ superscriptрқ•ҢвҖ \mathbb{U}^{\dagger} of unitary matrices in рқҗ‘dГ—dsuperscriptрқҗ‘рқ‘‘рқ‘‘\mathbf{R}^{d\times d} such that any two elements in рқ•ҢвҖ superscriptрқ•ҢвҖ \mathbb{U}^{\dagger} are sufficiently far. Then we can construct в„•вҖ ={UвҖ вҖӢLвҖ :UвҖ вҲҲрқ•Ң}superscriptв„•вҖ conditional-setsuperscriptрқ‘ҲвҖ superscriptрқҗҝвҖ superscriptрқ‘ҲвҖ рқ•Ң\mathbb{N}^{\dagger}=\{U^{\dagger}L^{\dagger}:U^{\dagger}\in\mathbb{U}\}.

We next reiterate (with elaboration) the challenge we face when using existing techniques. Then we describe our approach.We shall first examine a simple case, in which we need only design vectors for one column. Then we explain the difficulties of using an existing technique to generalize the design. Finally, we explain our solution.

Recall that (рқҗҷвҖ )TвҖӢрқҗҳ=(NвҖ )T+в„°superscriptsuperscriptрқҗҷвҖ Tрқҗҳsuperscriptsuperscriptрқ‘ҒвҖ Tв„°(\mathbf{Z}^{\dagger})^{\mathrm{T}}\mathbf{Y}=(N^{\dagger})^{\mathrm{T}}+\mathcal{E}, where we can roughly view в„°в„°\mathcal{E} as a matrix that consists of independent Gaussian (0,ПғПө/n)0subscriptрқңҺitalic-Пөрқ‘ӣ(0,\sigma_{\epsilon}/\sqrt{n}).For the sake of discussion, we assume ПғПө=1subscriptрқңҺitalic-Пө1\sigma_{\epsilon}=1 in our discussion below.

Warmup: one colume case.  The problem of packing one column roughly corresponds to establishing a lower bound on the estimation problemрқҗІ=рқҗ®+ПөрқҗІрқҗ®italic-Пө\mathbf{y}=\mathbf{u}+\epsilon, where рқҗІ,рқҗ®,ПөвҲҲрқҗ‘dрқҗІрқҗ®italic-Пөsuperscriptрқҗ‘рқ‘‘\mathbf{y},\mathbf{u},\epsilon\in\mathbf{R}^{d}. Пөitalic-Пө\epsilon corresponds to a column in в„°в„°\mathcal{E} and consists of dрқ‘‘d independent Gaussian NвҖӢ(0,1/n)рқ‘Ғ01рқ‘ӣN(0,1/\sqrt{n}).рқҗ®рқҗ®\mathbf{u} correpsonds to a column in UвҖ superscriptрқ‘ҲвҖ U^{\dagger} and we require вҖ–рқҗ®вҖ–2вүҲПҒвҖӢd/nsubscriptnormрқҗ®2рқңҢрқ‘‘рқ‘ӣ\|\mathbf{u}\|_{2}\approx\rho\sqrt{d/n}. To apply TheoremВ 2, we shallconstruct a рқ”»={рқҗ®1,вҖҰ,рқҗ®K}рқ”»subscriptрқҗ®1вҖҰsubscriptрқҗ®рқҗҫ\mathbb{D}=\{\mathbf{u}_{1},\dots,\mathbf{u}_{K}\} such that вҖ–рқҗ®iвҲ’рқҗ®jвҖ–normsubscriptрқҗ®рқ‘–subscriptрқҗ®рқ‘—\|\mathbf{u}_{i}-\mathbf{u}_{j}\| is large for each {i,j}рқ‘–рқ‘—\{i,j\} pair and KрқҗҫK is also large. Specifically, we require вҖ–рқҗ®iвҲ’рқҗ®jвҖ–22вүҲ2вҖӢПҒ2вҖӢdnsubscriptsuperscriptnormsubscriptрқҗ®рқ‘–subscriptрқҗ®рқ‘—222superscriptрқңҢ2рқ‘‘рқ‘ӣ\|\mathbf{u}_{i}-\mathbf{u}_{j}\|^{2}_{2}\approx 2\rho^{2}\frac{d}{n} (large distance requirement) andK=expвҒЎ(ОҳвҖӢ(ПҒвҖӢd))рқҗҫОҳрқңҢрқ‘‘K=\exp(\Theta(\sqrt{\rho}d)) (large set requirement). ПҒрқңҢ\sqrt{\rho} is carefully optimized and we will defer the reasoning to the full analysis below.A standard tool to construct рқ”»рқ”»\mathbb{D} is to use a probabilistic method. We sample рқҗ®isubscriptрқҗ®рқ‘–\mathbf{u}_{i} independently from the same distribution and argue that with high probability вҖ–рқҗ®iвҲ’рқҗ®jвҖ–22subscriptsuperscriptnormsubscriptрқҗ®рқ‘–subscriptрқҗ®рқ‘—22\|\mathbf{u}_{i}-\mathbf{u}_{j}\|^{2}_{2} is sufficiently large.Then a union bound can be used to derive KрқҗҫK. For example, we may set рқҗ®iвҲјNвҖӢ(0,ПҒвҖӢdnвҖӢIdГ—d)similar-tosubscriptрқҗ®рқ‘–рқ‘Ғ0рқңҢрқ‘‘рқ‘ӣsubscriptрқҗјрқ‘‘рқ‘‘\mathbf{u}_{i}\sim N(0,\rho\sqrt{\frac{d}{n}}I_{d\times d}) for all iрқ‘–i, and the concentration quality suffices for us to sample KрқҗҫK vectors.

Multiple column case.  We now move to the problem of packing multiple columns in Uрқ‘ҲU together. KрқҗҫK is required to be much larger, e.g., K=expвҒЎ(ОҳвҖӢ(ПҒвҖӢd2))рқҗҫОҳрқңҢsuperscriptрқ‘‘2K=\exp(\Theta(\sqrt{\rho}d^{2}))for certain problem instances. A natural generalization of one-column case is to build our parameter set by taking the Cartesian product of multiple copies of рқ”»рқ”»\mathbb{D}. This gives us a large KрқҗҫK for free but the key issue isthat vectors in рқ”»рқ”»\mathbb{D} are generated independently. So there is no way to guarantee they are independent to each other. In fact, it is straightforward to show that many elements in the Cartesian product are far from unitary.One may also directly sample random unitary matrices and argue that they are far from each other. But there seems to exist no tool that enables us to build up a concentration of expвҒЎ(вҲ’ОҳвҖӢ(ПҒвҖӢd2))ОҳрқңҢsuperscriptрқ‘‘2\exp(-\Theta(\sqrt{\rho}d^{2}))between two random unitary matrices.

Therefore, a fundamental problem is that we need independence to build up a large set but the unitary constraint limits the independence. So we either cannot satisfythe unitary requirement (Cartesian product approach) or cannot properly use the independence to build concentrations (random unitary matrix approach).

Our approach.  We develop a technique that decouples the three requirements (unitary matrices, large distance, and large KрқҗҫK). Let us re-examine the Cartesian product approach. When the vectors for each column are completely determined, then it is remarkably difficult to build a Cartesian product that guaranteesorthogonality between columns. To address this issue, our approach only вҖңpartiallyвҖқ specify vectors in each column. Then we take a Cartesian product of these partial specifications.So the size of the Cartesian product is sufficiently large; meanwhile an element in the product does not fully specify UвҖ superscriptрқ‘ҲвҖ U^{\dagger} so we still have room to make them unitary.Thus, our final step is to transform each partial specification in the Cartesian product into a unitary matrix. Specifically, it consists of three steps (See Fig.В 3)

Step 1. Partial specification of each column.  For each column iрқ‘–i of interest, we build up a collection рқ”»(i)={R(i,1),вҖҰ,R(i,K)}superscriptрқ”»рқ‘–superscriptрқ‘…рқ‘–1вҖҰsuperscriptрқ‘…рқ‘–рқҗҫ\mathbb{D}^{(i)}=\{R^{(i,1)},\dots,R^{(i,K)}\}. Each R(i,j)вҠӮ[d]superscriptрқ‘…рқ‘–рқ‘—delimited-[]рқ‘‘R^{(i,j)}\subset[d]specifies only the positions of non-zero entire for a vector prepared for filling in U:,isubscriptрқ‘Ҳ:рқ‘–U_{:,i}.

Step 2. Cartesian product.  Then we randomly sample elements from the Cartesian product рқ”»вүңвЁӮiрқ”»(i)вүңрқ”»subscripttensor-productрқ‘–superscriptрқ”»рқ‘–\mathbb{D}\triangleq\bigotimes_{i}\mathbb{D}^{(i)}. Each element in the product specifies the non-zero entries of UвҖ superscriptрқ‘ҲвҖ U^{\dagger}.We need to do another random sampling instead of using the full Cartesian product because we need to guarantee that any two matrices share a small number of non-zero entries.For example, (R(1,1),R(2,1),R(3,1))superscriptрқ‘…11superscriptрқ‘…21superscriptрқ‘…31(R^{(1,1)},R^{(2,1)},R^{(3,1)}) and (R(1,1),R(2,1),R(3,2))superscriptрқ‘…11superscriptрқ‘…21superscriptрқ‘…32(R^{(1,1)},R^{(2,1)},R^{(3,2)}) are two elements in вЁӮiрқ”»(i)subscripttensor-productрқ‘–superscriptрқ”»рқ‘–\bigotimes_{i}\mathbb{D}^{(i)} but they specify two matriceswith the same locations of non-zero entries for the first two columns.

Step 3. Building up unitary matrices.  Finally, for each element RвҶ’вҲҲрқ”»вҶ’рқ‘…рқ”»\vec{R}\in\mathbb{D} (that specify positions of non-zero entries), we carefully fill in the values of the non-zero entries so that all our matrices are unitary and far from each other.We shall show that it is always possible to construct unitary matrices that вҖңcomply withвҖқ RвҶ’вҶ’рқ‘…\vec{R}. In addition, our unitary matrices have few entries with large magnitude so when two matrices share few positions of non-zero entries, they are far.

We now execute the plan outlined in the roadmap. Let KрқҗҫK and О»рқңҶ\lambda be tunable parameters. For the purpose of getting intuition,KрқҗҫK is related to the size of рқ•ҢвҖ superscriptрқ•ҢвҖ \mathbb{U}^{\dagger} so it can be thought as being exponential in dрқ‘‘d, whereas О»рқңҶ\lambda is a constant and we use ПҒО»superscriptрқңҢрқңҶ\rho^{\lambda}to control the density of non-zero entries in each UвҖ вҲҲрқ•ҢвҖ superscriptрқ‘ҲвҖ superscriptрқ•ҢвҖ U^{\dagger}\in\mathbb{U}^{\dagger}.

Let рқ”»(i)={R(i,1),R(i,2),вӢҜ,R(i,K)}superscriptрқ”»рқ‘–superscriptрқ‘…рқ‘–1superscriptрқ‘…рқ‘–2вӢҜsuperscriptрқ‘…рқ‘–рқҗҫ\mathbb{D}^{(i)}=\{R^{(i,1)},R^{(i,2)},\cdots,R^{(i,K)}\} be a collection of random subsets in [d]delimited-[]рқ‘‘[d], in which each R(i,j)superscriptрқ‘…рқ‘–рқ‘—R^{(i,j)}is of size ПҒО»вҖӢdsuperscriptрқңҢрқңҶрқ‘‘\rho^{\lambda}d. We sample the subsets without replacement. Recall that tВҜВҜрқ‘Ў\underline{t} is the smallest index such that ПғtВҜвҖ вүӨПҒвҖӢПғПөвҖӢdnsubscriptsuperscriptрқңҺвҖ ВҜрқ‘ЎрқңҢsubscriptрқңҺitalic-Пөрқ‘‘рқ‘ӣ\sigma^{\dagger}_{\underline{t}}\leq\rho\sigma_{\epsilon}\sqrt{\frac{d}{n}}and let us also define tВҜ=вҢҠПҒО»вҖӢd2вҢӢВҜрқ‘ЎsuperscriptрқңҢрқңҶрқ‘‘2\overline{t}=\lfloor\frac{\rho^{\lambda}d}{2}\rfloor. We let Оі=tВҜвҲ’tВҜ+1рқӣҫВҜрқ‘ЎВҜрқ‘Ў1\gamma=\overline{t}-\underline{t}+1. We assume that tВҜвүҘtВҜВҜрқ‘ЎВҜрқ‘Ў\overline{t}\geq\underline{t}; otherwise PropositionВ 3 becomes trivial. Letрқ”»рқ”»\mathbb{D} be the Cartesian product of рқ”»(i)superscriptрқ”»рқ‘–\mathbb{D}^{(i)} for integers iвҲҲ[tВҜ,tВҜ]рқ‘–ВҜрқ‘ЎВҜрқ‘Ўi\in[\underline{t},\overline{t}]. We use RвҶ’вҶ’рқ‘…\vec{R} to denote an element in рқ”»рқ”»\mathbb{D}. RвҶ’=(RвҶ’tВҜ,RвҶ’tВҜ+1,вӢҜ,RвҶ’tВҜ)вҶ’рқ‘…subscriptвҶ’рқ‘…ВҜрқ‘ЎsubscriptвҶ’рқ‘…ВҜрқ‘Ў1вӢҜsubscriptвҶ’рқ‘…ВҜрқ‘Ў\vec{R}=(\vec{R}_{\underline{t}},\vec{R}_{\underline{t}+1},\cdots,\vec{R}_{\overline{t}}) is aОірқӣҫ\gamma-tuple so that each element RвҶ’isubscriptвҶ’рқ‘…рқ‘–\vec{R}_{i} corresponds to an element in рқ”»(i)superscriptрқ”»рқ‘–\mathbb{D}^{(i)}. There are two ways to represent RвҶ’вҶ’рқ‘…\vec{R}. Both are found useful in our analysis.

1.Set representation. We treat RвҶ’isubscriptвҶ’рқ‘…рқ‘–\vec{R}_{i} as a set in рқ”»(i)superscriptрқ”»рқ‘–\mathbb{D}^{(i)}.2.Index representation. We treat RвҶ’isubscriptвҶ’рқ‘…рқ‘–\vec{R}_{i} as an index from [K]delimited-[]рқҗҫ[K] that specifies the index of the set that RвҶ’isubscriptвҶ’рқ‘…рқ‘–\vec{R}_{i} refers to. 

Note that the subscript iрқ‘–i of RвҶ’isubscriptвҶ’рқ‘…рқ‘–\vec{R}_{i} starts at tВҜВҜрқ‘Ў\underline{t} (instead of 111 or 00) for convenience.

We now describe our proof in detail. We remark that throughout our analysis, constants are re-used in different proofs.

This step needs only characterize the behavior of an individual рқ”»(i)superscriptрқ”»рқ‘–\mathbb{D}^{(i)}.

This can be proved by a standard probabilistic argument.Let R(i,j)superscriptрқ‘…рқ‘–рқ‘—R^{(i,j)} be an arbitrary subset such that |R(i,j)|=ПҒО»вҖӢdsuperscriptрқ‘…рқ‘–рқ‘—superscriptрқңҢрқңҶрқ‘‘|R^{(i,j)}|=\rho^{\lambda}d. Let R(i,k)superscriptрқ‘…рқ‘–рқ‘ҳR^{(i,k)} be a random subset of size ПҒО»вҖӢdsuperscriptрқңҢрқңҶрқ‘‘\rho^{\lambda}d. We computethe probability that |R(i,j)вҲ©R(i,k)|вүҘc2вҖӢПҒ2вҖӢО»вҖӢdsuperscriptрқ‘…рқ‘–рқ‘—superscriptрқ‘…рқ‘–рқ‘ҳsubscriptрқ‘җ2superscriptрқңҢ2рқңҶрқ‘‘|R^{(i,j)}\cap R^{(i,k)}|\geq c_{2}\rho^{2\lambda}d for a fixed R(i,j)superscriptрқ‘…рқ‘–рқ‘—R^{(i,j)}.

Let us sequentially sample elements from R(i,k)superscriptрқ‘…рқ‘–рқ‘ҳR^{(i,k)} (without replacement). Let Itsubscriptрқҗјрқ‘ЎI_{t} be an indicator random variable that sets to 1 if and only ifthe tрқ‘Ўt-th random element in R(i,k)superscriptрқ‘…рқ‘–рқ‘ҳR^{(i,k)} hits an element in R(i,j)superscriptрқ‘…рқ‘–рқ‘—R^{(i,j)}. We havePrвҒЎ[It=1]вүӨПҒО»вҖӢd(1вҲ’ПҒО»)вҖӢdвүӨПҒО»2.Prsubscriptрқҗјрқ‘Ў1superscriptрқңҢрқңҶрқ‘‘1superscriptрқңҢрқңҶрқ‘‘superscriptрқңҢрқңҶ2\Pr[I_{t}=1]\leq\frac{\rho^{\lambda}d}{(1-\rho^{\lambda})d}\leq\frac{\rho^{\lambda}}{2}.(39)By using a Chernoff bound, we havePrвҒЎ[|вҲ‘i=1ПҒО»вҖӢdIt|вүҘc2вҖӢПҒ2вҖӢО»вҖӢd2]вүӨexpвҒЎ(вҲ’О©вҖӢ(ПҒ2вҖӢО»вҖӢd)).Prsuperscriptsubscriptрқ‘–1superscriptрқңҢрқңҶрқ‘‘subscriptрқҗјрқ‘Ўsubscriptрқ‘җ2superscriptрқңҢ2рқңҶрқ‘‘2О©superscriptрқңҢ2рқңҶрқ‘‘\Pr\left[|\sum_{i=1}^{\rho^{\lambda}d}I_{t}|\geq\frac{c_{2}\rho^{2\lambda}d}{2}\right]\leq\exp(-\Omega(\rho^{2\lambda}d)).(40)By using a union bound, we havePrвҒЎ[вҲғi,j:|R(i,j)вҲ©R(i,k)|вүҘc2вҖӢПҒ2вҖӢО»вҖӢd2]вүӨ(K2)вҖӢexpвҒЎ(вҲ’О©вҖӢ(ПҒ2вҖӢО»вҖӢd))вүӨexpвҒЎ(вҲ’О©вҖӢ(ПҒ2вҖӢО»вҖӢd)+2вҖӢlogвҒЎK).Prрқ‘–:рқ‘—superscriptрқ‘…рқ‘–рқ‘—superscriptрқ‘…рқ‘–рқ‘ҳsubscriptрқ‘җ2superscriptрқңҢ2рқңҶрқ‘‘2binomialрқҗҫ2О©superscriptрқңҢ2рқңҶрқ‘‘О©superscriptрқңҢ2рқңҶрқ‘‘2рқҗҫ\Pr[\exists i,j:|R^{(i,j)}\cap R^{(i,k)}|\geq\frac{c_{2}\rho^{2\lambda}d}{2}]\leq\binom{K}{2}\exp(-\Omega(\rho^{2\lambda}d))\leq\exp(-\Omega(\rho^{2\lambda}d)+2\log K).(41)Therefore, when we set K=expвҒЎ(c0вҖӢПҒ2вҖӢО»вҖӢd)рқҗҫsubscriptрқ‘җ0superscriptрқңҢ2рқңҶрқ‘‘K=\exp(c_{0}\rho^{2\lambda}d), the failure probability is 1вҲ’expвҒЎ(вҲ’ОҳвҖӢ(ПҒ2вҖӢО»вҖӢd))1ОҳsuperscriptрқңҢ2рқңҶрқ‘‘1-\exp(-\Theta(\rho^{2\lambda}d)).вҲҺ

We let рқ”»=вЁӮiвҲҲ[tВҜ,tВҜ]рқ”»(i)рқ”»subscripttensor-productрқ‘–ВҜрқ‘ЎВҜрқ‘Ўsuperscriptрқ”»рқ‘–\mathbb{D}=\bigotimes_{i\in[\underline{t},\overline{t}]}\mathbb{D}^{(i)}. Note that each рқ”»(i)superscriptрқ”»рқ‘–\mathbb{D}^{(i)} is sampled independently. We define рқ•Ҡрқ•Ҡ\mathbb{S} be a random subset of рқ”»рқ”»\mathbb{D}. We next explain the reason we need to sample random subsets. Recall that for each RвҶ’вҲҲрқ•ҠвҶ’рқ‘…рқ•Ҡ\vec{R}\in\mathbb{S}, we aim to construct a unitary matrix UвҖ superscriptрқ‘ҲвҖ U^{\dagger} (to be discussed in Step 3) such that the positions of non-zero entries in U:,iвҖ subscriptsuperscriptрқ‘ҲвҖ :рқ‘–U^{\dagger}_{:,i} are specified by RвҶ’isubscriptвҶ’рқ‘…рқ‘–\vec{R}_{i} (i.e., Uj,iвҖ вү 0subscriptsuperscriptрқ‘ҲвҖ рқ‘—рқ‘–0U^{\dagger}_{j,i}\neq 0 only when jвҲҲRвҶ’iрқ‘—subscriptвҶ’рқ‘…рқ‘–j\in\vec{R}_{i}).

Let RвҶ’вҶ’рқ‘…\vec{R} and RвҶ’вҖІsuperscriptвҶ’рқ‘…вҖІ\vec{R}^{\prime} be two distinct elements in рқ”»рқ”»\mathbb{D}. Let UвҖ superscriptрқ‘ҲвҖ U^{\dagger} and U~вҖ superscript~рқ‘ҲвҖ \tilde{U}^{\dagger} be two unitary matrices generated by RвҶ’вҶ’рқ‘…\vec{R} and RвҶ’вҖІsuperscriptвҶ’рқ‘…вҖІ\vec{R}^{\prime}. We ultimately aim to have that вҖ–UвҖ вҖӢLвҖ вҲ’U~вҖ вҖӢLвҖ вҖ–F2subscriptsuperscriptnormsuperscriptрқ‘ҲвҖ superscriptрқҗҝвҖ superscript~рқ‘ҲвҖ superscriptрқҗҝвҖ 2рқҗ№\|U^{\dagger}L^{\dagger}-\tilde{U}^{\dagger}L^{\dagger}\|^{2}_{F} being large. We shall make sure (i) UвҖ superscriptрқ‘ҲвҖ U^{\dagger} and U~вҖ superscript~рқ‘ҲвҖ \tilde{U}^{\dagger} share few non-zero positions (Step 2; this step), and (ii) few entries in UвҖ superscriptрқ‘ҲвҖ U^{\dagger} and U~вҖ superscript~рқ‘ҲвҖ \tilde{U}^{\dagger} have excessive magnitude (Step 3). These two conditions will imply that UвҖ superscriptрқ‘ҲвҖ U^{\dagger} and U~вҖ superscript~рқ‘ҲвҖ \tilde{U}^{\dagger} are far, which then implies a lower bound on UвҖ вҖӢLвҖ superscriptрқ‘ҲвҖ superscriptрқҗҝвҖ U^{\dagger}L^{\dagger} and U~вҖ вҖӢLвҖ superscript~рқ‘ҲвҖ superscriptрқҗҝвҖ \tilde{U}^{\dagger}L^{\dagger}.

Because we do not want UвҖ superscriptрқ‘ҲвҖ U^{\dagger} and U~вҖ superscript~рқ‘ҲвҖ \tilde{U}^{\dagger} share non-zero positions, we want to maximize the Hamming distance (in index representation) between RвҶ’вҶ’рқ‘…\vec{R} and RвҶ’вҖІsuperscriptвҶ’рқ‘…вҖІ\vec{R}^{\prime} (i.e., RвҶ’i=RвҶ’iвҖІsubscriptвҶ’рқ‘…рқ‘–subscriptsuperscriptвҶ’рқ‘…вҖІрқ‘–\vec{R}_{i}=\vec{R}^{\prime}_{i} implies U:,iвҖ subscriptsuperscriptрқ‘ҲвҖ :рқ‘–U^{\dagger}_{:,i} and U~:,iвҖ subscriptsuperscript~рқ‘ҲвҖ :рқ‘–\tilde{U}^{\dagger}_{:,i} share all non-zero positions, which is a bad event). We sample рқ•Ҡрқ•Ҡ\mathbb{S} randomly from рқ”»рқ”»\mathbb{D} because random sample is a known procedure that generates вҖңcodeвҖқ with large Hamming distanceВ mackay2003information .

Before proceeding, we note one catch in the above explanation, i.e., differentcolumns are of different importance. Specifically, вҖ–UвҖ вҖӢLвҖ вҲ’U~вҖ вҖӢLвҖ вҖ–F2=вҲ‘iвҲҲ[d](ПғiвҖ )2вҖӢвҖ–U:,iвҖ вҲ’U~:,iвҖ вҖ–2subscriptsuperscriptnormsuperscriptрқ‘ҲвҖ superscriptрқҗҝвҖ superscript~рқ‘ҲвҖ superscriptрқҗҝвҖ 2рқҗ№subscriptрқ‘–delimited-[]рқ‘‘superscriptsubscriptsuperscriptрқңҺвҖ рқ‘–2superscriptnormsubscriptsuperscriptрқ‘ҲвҖ :рқ‘–subscriptsuperscript~рқ‘ҲвҖ :рқ‘–2\|U^{\dagger}L^{\dagger}-\tilde{U}^{\dagger}L^{\dagger}\|^{2}_{F}=\sum_{i\in[d]}(\sigma^{\dagger}_{i})^{2}\|U^{\dagger}_{:,i}-\tilde{U}^{\dagger}_{:,i}\|^{2}. When RвҶ’isubscriptвҶ’рқ‘…рқ‘–\vec{R}_{i} and RвҶ’iвҖІsubscriptsuperscriptвҶ’рқ‘…вҖІрқ‘–\vec{R}^{\prime}_{i} collide for a large (ПғiвҖ )2superscriptsubscriptsuperscriptрқңҺвҖ рқ‘–2(\sigma^{\dagger}_{i})^{2}, it makes more impact to the Frobenius norm. Thus, we define a weighted cost function that resembles the structure of Hamming distance.

рқҗңвҖӢ(RвҶ’,RвҶ’вҖІ)=вҲ‘iвҲҲ[tВҜ,tВҜ](ПғiвҖ )2вҖӢIвҖӢ(RвҶ’i=RвҶ’iвҖІ).рқҗңвҶ’рқ‘…superscriptвҶ’рқ‘…вҖІsubscriptрқ‘–ВҜрқ‘ЎВҜрқ‘ЎsuperscriptsubscriptsuperscriptрқңҺвҖ рқ‘–2рқҗјsubscriptвҶ’рқ‘…рқ‘–subscriptsuperscriptвҶ’рқ‘…вҖІрқ‘–\mathbf{c}(\vec{R},\vec{R}^{\prime})=\sum_{i\in[\underline{t},\overline{t}]}(\sigma^{\dagger}_{i})^{2}I(\vec{R}_{i}=\vec{R}^{\prime}_{i}).(42)

Note that the direction we need for рқҗңвҖӢ(RвҶ’,RвҶ’вҖІ)рқҗңвҶ’рқ‘…superscriptвҶ’рқ‘…вҖІ\mathbf{c}(\vec{R},\vec{R}^{\prime}) is opposite to Hamming distance. One usually maximizes Hamming distance whereas we need to minimize the weighted cost.

We need to develop a specialized technique to produce concentration behavior for рқ•Ҡрқ•Ҡ\mathbb{S} because рқҗңвҖӢ(RвҶ’,RвҶ’вҖІ)рқҗңвҶ’рқ‘…superscriptвҶ’рқ‘…вҖІ\mathbf{c}(\vec{R},\vec{R}^{\prime}) is weighted.
