We next construct a set of unitary matrices in рқҗ‘dГ—dsuperscriptрқҗ‘рқ‘‘рқ‘‘\mathbf{R}^{d\times d} based on elements in рқ•Ҡрқ•Ҡ\mathbb{S}.We shall refer to the procedure to generate a unitary Uрқ‘ҲU from an element RвҶ’вҲҲрқ•ҠвҶ’рқ‘…рқ•Ҡ\vec{R}\in\mathbb{S} as qвҖӢ(RвҶ’)рқ‘һвҶ’рқ‘…q(\vec{R}).

Procedure qвҖӢ(RвҶ’)рқ‘һвҶ’рқ‘…q(\vec{R}):  Let UвҲҲрқҗ‘dГ—dрқ‘Ҳsuperscriptрқҗ‘рқ‘‘рқ‘‘U\in\mathbf{R}^{d\times d} be the matrix qвҖӢ(RвҶ’)рқ‘һвҶ’рқ‘…q(\vec{R}) aims to fill in.Let рқҗҜ(1),рқҗҜ(2),вҖҰ,рқҗҜ(tВҜвҲ’1)вҲҲрқҗ‘dsuperscriptрқҗҜ1superscriptрқҗҜ2вҖҰsuperscriptрқҗҜВҜрқ‘Ў1superscriptрқҗ‘рқ‘‘\mathbf{v}^{(1)},\mathbf{v}^{(2)},\dots,\mathbf{v}^{(\underline{t}-1)}\in\mathbf{R}^{d} be an arbitrary set of orthonormal vectors.qвҖӢ(RвҶ’)рқ‘һвҶ’рқ‘…q(\vec{R}) partitions the matrix Uрқ‘ҲU into three regions of columns and it fills different regions with different strategies. See also three regions illustrated by matrices in Fig.В 3.

Region 1: U:,isubscriptрқ‘Ҳ:рқ‘–U_{:,i} for i<tВҜрқ‘–ВҜрқ‘Ўi<\underline{t}.  We set U:,i=рқҗҜ(i)subscriptрқ‘Ҳ:рқ‘–superscriptрқҗҜрқ‘–U_{:,i}=\mathbf{v}^{(i)} when i<tВҜрқ‘–ВҜрқ‘Ўi<\underline{t}. This means all the unitary matrices we constructshare the first tВҜвҲ’1ВҜрқ‘Ў1\underline{t}-1 columns.

Region 2: U:,isubscriptрқ‘Ҳ:рқ‘–U_{:,i} for iвҲҲ[tВҜ,tВҜ]рқ‘–ВҜрқ‘ЎВҜрқ‘Ўi\in[\underline{t},\overline{t}].  We next fill in non-zero entries of each U:,isubscriptрқ‘Ҳ:рқ‘–U_{:,i} by RвҶ’isubscriptвҶ’рқ‘…рқ‘–\vec{R}_{i} for iвҲҲ[tВҜ,tВҜ]рқ‘–ВҜрқ‘ЎВҜрқ‘Ўi\in[\underline{t},\overline{t}]. We fill in each U:,isubscriptрқ‘Ҳ:рқ‘–U_{:,i}sequentially from left to right (from small iрқ‘–i to large iрқ‘–i). We need to make sure that (i) it is feasible to construct U:,isubscriptрқ‘Ҳ:рқ‘–U_{:,i} that is orthogonal to all U:.jU_{:.j} (j<iрқ‘—рқ‘–j<i)by using only entries specified by Risubscriptрқ‘…рқ‘–R_{i}. (ii) there is a way to fill in U:,isubscriptрқ‘Ҳ:рқ‘–U_{:,i} so that not too many entries are excessively large. (ii) is needed becausefor any RвҶ’вҶ’рқ‘…\vec{R} and RвҶ’вҖІsuperscriptвҶ’рқ‘…вҖІ\vec{R}^{\prime}, RвҶ’isubscriptвҶ’рқ‘…рқ‘–\vec{R}_{i} and RвҶ’iвҖІsubscriptsuperscriptвҶ’рқ‘…вҖІрқ‘–\vec{R}^{\prime}_{i} still share a small number of non-zero positions (whp |RвҶ’iвҲ©RвҶ’iвҖІ|=OвҖӢ(ПҒ2вҖӢО»вҖӢd)subscriptвҶ’рқ‘…рқ‘–subscriptsuperscriptвҶ’рқ‘…вҖІрқ‘–рқ‘ӮsuperscriptрқңҢ2рқңҶрқ‘‘|\vec{R}_{i}\cap\vec{R}^{\prime}_{i}|=O(\rho^{2\lambda}d), according to LemmaВ 11). When the mass in |RвҶ’iвҲ©RвҶ’iвҖІ|subscriptвҶ’рқ‘…рқ‘–subscriptsuperscriptвҶ’рқ‘…вҖІрқ‘–|\vec{R}_{i}\cap\vec{R}^{\prime}_{i}| is large, the distance between Uрқ‘ҲU and UвҖІsuperscriptрқ‘ҲвҖІU^{\prime} is harder to control.

Region 3: U:,isubscriptрқ‘Ҳ:рқ‘–U_{:,i} for i>tВҜрқ‘–ВҜрқ‘Ўi>\overline{t}. qвҖӢ(RвҶ’)рқ‘һвҶ’рқ‘…q(\vec{R}) fills in the rest of the vectors arbitrarily so long as Uрқ‘ҲU is unitary. Unlike the first tВҜвҲ’1ВҜрқ‘Ў1\underline{t}-1 columns, these columns depend on RвҶ’вҶ’рқ‘…\vec{R} so each UвҲҲрқ•Ңрқ‘Ҳрқ•ҢU\in\mathbb{U} has a different set of ending column vectors.

Analysis for region 2.  Our analysis focuses on two asserted properties for Region 2 are true. We first show (i) is true and describe a procedure to make sure (ii) happens.

For jвүӨiвҲ’1рқ‘—рқ‘–1j\leq i-1, let рқҗ°(j)вҲҲрқҗ‘ПҒО»вҖӢdsuperscriptрқҗ°рқ‘—superscriptрқҗ‘superscriptрқңҢрқңҶрқ‘‘\mathbf{w}^{(j)}\in\mathbf{R}^{\rho^{\lambda}d} be the projection of U:,jsubscriptрқ‘Ҳ:рқ‘—U_{:,j} onto the coordinates specified by RвҶ’isubscriptвҶ’рқ‘…рқ‘–\vec{R}_{i}. See Fig.В 3(d) for an illustration.Note that tВҜ=ПҒО»вҖӢd2ВҜрқ‘ЎsuperscriptрқңҢрқңҶрқ‘‘2\overline{t}=\frac{\rho^{\lambda}d}{2}, the dimension of the subspace spanned by рқҗ°(1),вҖҰвҖӢрқҗ°(iвҲ’1)superscriptрқҗ°1вҖҰsuperscriptрқҗ°рқ‘–1\mathbf{w}^{(1)},\dots\mathbf{w}^{(i-1)} is at most ПҒО»вҖӢd/2superscriptрқңҢрқңҶрқ‘‘2\rho^{\lambda}d/2.Therefore, we can find a set of orthonormal vectors {рқҗ®(1),вҖҰвҖӢрқҗ®(Оә)}вҠҶрқҗ‘ПҒО»вҖӢdsuperscriptрқҗ®1вҖҰsuperscriptрқҗ®рқң…superscriptрқҗ‘superscriptрқңҢрқңҶрқ‘‘\{\mathbf{u}^{(1)},\dots\mathbf{u}^{(\kappa)}\}\subseteq\mathbf{R}^{\rho^{\lambda}d} (ОәвүҘПҒО»вҖӢd2рқң…superscriptрқңҢрқңҶрқ‘‘2\kappa\geq\frac{\rho^{\lambda}d}{2}) that are orthogonal to рқҗ°(j)superscriptрқҗ°рқ‘—\mathbf{w}^{(j)} (jвүӨiвҲ’1рқ‘—рқ‘–1j\leq i-1).To build a U:,isubscriptрқ‘Ҳ:рқ‘–U_{:,i} thatвҖҷs orthogonal to all U:,jsubscriptрқ‘Ҳ:рқ‘—U_{:,j} (jвүӨiвҲ’1рқ‘—рқ‘–1j\leq i-1), we can first find a рқҗ®вҲҲрқҗ‘ПҒО»вҖӢdрқҗ®superscriptрқҗ‘superscriptрқңҢрқңҶрқ‘‘\mathbf{u}\in\mathbf{R}^{\rho^{\lambda}d} that is a linear combination of {рқҗ®(j)}jвүӨОәsubscriptsuperscriptрқҗ®рқ‘—рқ‘—рқң…\{\mathbf{u}^{(j)}\}_{j\leq\kappa}, and then вҖңinflateвҖқ рқҗ®рқҗ®\mathbf{u}back to рқҗ‘dsuperscriptрқҗ‘рқ‘‘\mathbf{R}^{d}, i.e., the kрқ‘ҳk-th non-zero coordinate of U:,isubscriptрқ‘Ҳ:рқ‘–U_{:,i} is рқҗ®ksubscriptрқҗ®рқ‘ҳ\mathbf{u}_{k}. One can see thatвҹЁU:,j,U:,iвҹ©=вҹЁрқҗ°(j),рқҗ®вҹ©=0subscriptрқ‘Ҳ:рқ‘—subscriptрқ‘Ҳ:рқ‘–superscriptрқҗ°рқ‘—рқҗ®0\displaystyle\langle U_{:,j},U_{:,i}\rangle=\langle\mathbf{w}^{(j)},\mathbf{u}\rangle=0for any j<iрқ‘—рқ‘–j<i.

We now make sure (ii) happens. We have the following Lemma.

We use a probabilistic method to find рқҗ®рқҗ®\mathbf{u}.Let ziвҲјNвҖӢ(0,1/ПҒО»вҖӢd)similar-tosubscriptрқ‘§рқ‘–рқ‘Ғ01superscriptрқңҢрқңҶрқ‘‘z_{i}\sim N(0,1/\sqrt{\rho^{\lambda}d}) for iвҲҲ[ПҒО»вҖӢd]рқ‘–delimited-[]superscriptрқңҢрқңҶрқ‘‘i\in[\rho^{\lambda}d].Let S=вҲ‘iвүӨПҒО»вҖӢdzi2рқ‘Ҷsubscriptрқ‘–superscriptрқңҢрқңҶрқ‘‘subscriptsuperscriptрқ‘§2рқ‘–S=\sqrt{\sum_{i\leq\rho^{\lambda}d}z^{2}_{i}}. We shall set ОІi=zi/SsubscriptрқӣҪрқ‘–subscriptрқ‘§рқ‘–рқ‘Ҷ\beta_{i}=z_{i}/S. One can check that рқҗ®=вҲ‘iвҲҲ[ПҒО»вҖӢd]ОІiвҖӢрқҗ®(i)рқҗ®subscriptрқ‘–delimited-[]superscriptрқңҢрқңҶрқ‘‘subscriptрқӣҪрқ‘–superscriptрқҗ®рқ‘–\mathbf{u}=\sum_{i\in[\rho^{\lambda}d]}\beta_{i}\mathbf{u}^{(i)}is a unit vector. We then examine whether (45) is satisfied for these ОІisubscriptрқӣҪрқ‘–\beta_{i}вҖҷs we created. If not, we re-generate a new set of zisubscriptрқ‘§рқ‘–z_{i}вҖҷs and ОІisubscriptрқӣҪрқ‘–\beta_{i}вҖҷs.We repeat this process until (45) is satisfied.

Because ОІisubscriptрқӣҪрқ‘–\beta_{i}вҖҷs are normalized, setting the standard deviation of zisubscriptрқ‘§рқ‘–z_{i} is unnecessary. Wenevertheless do so because Sрқ‘ҶS will be approximately a constant, which helps us simplify the calculation.

We claim that there exists a constant cрқ‘җc such that for any в„“в„“\ell,

IвҖӢEвҖӢ[рқҗ®в„“2вҖӢIвҖӢ(рқҗ®в„“вүҘc5ПҒО»+О·вҖӢd)]вүӨcвҖӢОҫПҒО»вҖӢd.IEdelimited-[]subscriptsuperscriptрқҗ®2в„“рқҗјsubscriptрқҗ®в„“subscriptрқ‘җ5superscriptрқңҢрқңҶрқңӮрқ‘‘рқ‘җрқңүsuperscriptрқңҢрқңҶрқ‘‘\mathrm{I\!E}\left[\mathbf{u}^{2}_{\ell}I\left(\mathbf{u}_{\ell}\geq\frac{c_{5}}{\sqrt{\rho^{\lambda+\eta}d}}\right)\right]\leq\frac{c\xi}{\rho^{\lambda}d}.(46)

We first show that (46) implies LemmaВ 13. Then we will show (46).

By linearity of expectation, (46) impliesIвҖӢEвҖӢ[вҲ‘в„“вүӨПҒО»вҖӢdрқҗ®в„“2вҖӢIвҖӢ(рқҗ®в„“вүҘc5ПҒО»+О·вҖӢd)]вүӨcвҖӢОҫ.IEdelimited-[]subscriptв„“superscriptрқңҢрқңҶрқ‘‘subscriptsuperscriptрқҗ®2в„“рқҗјsubscriptрқҗ®в„“subscriptрқ‘җ5superscriptрқңҢрқңҶрқңӮрқ‘‘рқ‘җрқңү\displaystyle\mathrm{I\!E}\left[\sum_{\ell\leq\rho^{\lambda}d}\mathbf{u}^{2}_{\ell}I\left(\mathbf{u}_{\ell}\geq\frac{c_{5}}{\sqrt{\rho^{\lambda+\eta}d}}\right)\right]\leq c\xi.Then we use a Markov inequality and obtainPrвҒЎ[(вҲ‘в„“вүӨПҒО»вҖӢdрқҗ®в„“2вҖӢIвҖӢ(рқҗ®в„“вүҘc5ПҒО»+О·вҖӢd))вүҘ2вҖӢcвҖӢОҫ]вүӨ12Prsubscriptв„“superscriptрқңҢрқңҶрқ‘‘subscriptsuperscriptрқҗ®2в„“рқҗјsubscriptрқҗ®в„“subscriptрқ‘җ5superscriptрқңҢрқңҶрқңӮрқ‘‘2рқ‘җрқңү12\displaystyle\Pr\left[\left(\sum_{\ell\leq\rho^{\lambda}d}\mathbf{u}^{2}_{\ell}I\left(\mathbf{u}_{\ell}\geq\frac{c_{5}}{\sqrt{\rho^{\lambda+\eta}d}}\right)\right)\geq 2c\xi\right]\leq\frac{1}{2}

So our probabilistic method described above is guaranteed to find a рқҗ®рқҗ®\mathbf{u} that satisfies (45)

We next move to showing (46). Recall thatрқҗ®в„“=1SвҖӢ(вҲ‘iвүӨОәziвҖӢрқҗ®в„“(i)).subscriptрқҗ®в„“1рқ‘Ҷsubscriptрқ‘–рқң…subscriptрқ‘§рқ‘–subscriptsuperscriptрқҗ®рқ‘–в„“\displaystyle\mathbf{u}_{\ell}=\frac{1}{S}(\sum_{i\leq\kappa}z_{i}\mathbf{u}^{(i)}_{\ell}).

We also let Zв„“=вҲ‘iвүӨОәziвҖӢрқҗ®в„“(i)subscriptрқ‘Қв„“subscriptрқ‘–рқң…subscriptрқ‘§рқ‘–subscriptsuperscriptрқҗ®рқ‘–в„“Z_{\ell}=\sum_{i\leq\kappa}z_{i}\mathbf{u}^{(i)}_{\ell}. n\mathrm{I\!E}_{\mathbf{z}}\left[\mathrm{KL}(\mathbf{P}_{N^{\dagger}\mid\mathbf{z}^{\dagger}},\mathbf{P}_{\tilde{N}^{\dagger}\mid\mathbf{z}^{\dagger}})\right]=\frac{n\|N^{\dagger}-\tilde{N}^{\dagger}\|^{2}_{F}}{2\sigma^{2}_{\epsilon}}вҲҺ

We now complete the proof for PropositionВ 3. First, define ПҲвүңвҲ‘iвүҘtВҜ+1(ПғiвҖ )2вҲ‘iвҲҲ[tВҜ,tВҜ](ПғiвҖ )2вүңрқң“subscriptрқ‘–ВҜрқ‘Ў1superscriptsubscriptsuperscriptрқңҺвҖ рқ‘–2subscriptрқ‘–ВҜрқ‘ЎВҜрқ‘ЎsuperscriptsubscriptsuperscriptрқңҺвҖ рқ‘–2\psi\triangleq\frac{\sum_{i\geq\overline{t}+1}(\sigma^{\dagger}_{i})^{2}}{\sum_{i\in[\underline{t},\overline{t}]}(\sigma^{\dagger}_{i})^{2}}. For anyNвҖ superscriptрқ‘ҒвҖ N^{\dagger} and N~вҖ superscript~рқ‘ҒвҖ \tilde{N}^{\dagger} in в„•в„•\mathbb{N}, we haveвҖ–NвҖ вҲ’N~вҖ вҖ–F2=вҲ‘iвүҘtВҜ(ПғiвҖ )2=(1+ПҲ)вҖӢОЁ,subscriptsuperscriptnormsuperscriptрқ‘ҒвҖ superscript~рқ‘ҒвҖ 2рқҗ№subscriptрқ‘–ВҜрқ‘ЎsuperscriptsubscriptsuperscriptрқңҺвҖ рқ‘–21рқң“ОЁ\|N^{\dagger}-\tilde{N}^{\dagger}\|^{2}_{F}=\sum_{i\geq\underline{t}}(\sigma^{\dagger}_{i})^{2}=(1+\psi)\Psi,where recall that ОЁ=вҲ‘iвҲҲ[tВҜ,tВҜ](ПғiвҖ )2ОЁsubscriptрқ‘–ВҜрқ‘ЎВҜрқ‘ЎsuperscriptsubscriptsuperscriptрқңҺвҖ рқ‘–2\Psi=\sum_{i\in[\underline{t},\overline{t}]}(\sigma^{\dagger}_{i})^{2}. Using LemmaВ 14, we have KLвҖӢ(рқҗҸNвҖ ,n,рқҗҸN~вҖ ,n)=nвҖӢ(1+ПҲ)вҖӢОЁKLsubscriptрқҗҸsuperscriptрқ‘ҒвҖ рқ‘ӣsubscriptрқҗҸsuperscript~рқ‘ҒвҖ рқ‘ӣрқ‘ӣ1рқң“ОЁ\mathrm{KL}(\mathbf{P}_{N^{\dagger},n},\mathbf{P}_{\tilde{N}^{\dagger},n})=n(1+\psi)\Psi.

In this section, we compare our results to other regression algorithms thatmake low rank constraints on Mрқ‘ҖM. The improvement here is twofold. First, our bound is directly characterized by Nрқ‘ҒN in orthogonalized form, whereas result ofВ negahban2011estimation needs to examine the interaction between Mрқ‘ҖM and CвҲ—superscriptрқҗ¶C^{*}, so their MSE depends onboth RqMsubscriptsuperscriptрқ‘…рқ‘Җрқ‘һR^{M}_{q} and О»minвҲ—subscriptsuperscriptрқңҶ\lambda^{*}_{\min}. Second, our bound no longer depends ond1subscriptрқ‘‘1d_{1} and pays only an additive factor nвҲ’c0superscriptрқ‘ӣsubscriptрқ‘җ0n^{-c_{0}}, thus, when n<d1рқ‘ӣsubscriptрқ‘‘1n<d_{1}, ourresult is significantly better. Other works have different parameters in theupper bounds, but all of these existing results require that n>d1рқ‘ӣsubscriptрқ‘‘1n>d_{1}to obtain non-trivial upperboundsВ koltchinskii2011nuclear ; bunea2011optimal ; chen2013reduced ; koltchinskii2011nuclear . Unlike these prior work, we require a stochastic assumption on рқҗ—рқҗ—\mathbf{X} (the rows are i.i.d.) to ensure that the model is identifiable when n<d1рқ‘ӣsubscriptрқ‘‘1n<d_{1}, e.g. there could be two sets of disjoint features that fit the training data equally well.Our algorithm produces an adaptive model whose complexity is controlled byk1subscriptрқ‘ҳ1k_{1} and k2subscriptрқ‘ҳ2k_{2}, which are adjusted dynamically depending on the sample sizeand noise level. bunea2011optimal  and chen2013reduced  also pointout the need for adaptivity; however they still require n>d1рқ‘ӣsubscriptрқ‘‘1n>d_{1} and makesome strong assumptions. For instance,bunea2011optimal assumes that there is a gap between ПғiвҖӢ(рқҗ—вҖӢMT)subscriptрқңҺрқ‘–рқҗ—superscriptрқ‘ҖT\sigma_{i}(\mathbf{X}M^{\mathrm{T}}) and Пғi+1вҖӢ(рқҗ—вҖӢMT)subscriptрқңҺрқ‘–1рқҗ—superscriptрқ‘ҖT\sigma_{i+1}(\mathbf{X}M^{\mathrm{T}}) for some iрқ‘–i. In comparison, our sufficient condition, the decay of О»iвҲ—subscriptsuperscriptрқңҶрқ‘–\lambda^{*}_{i}, is more natural.Our work is not directly comparable to standard variable selection techniques such as LASSOВ tibshirani1996regression  because they handle univariate рқҗІрқҗІ\mathbf{y}.Column selection algorithmsВ dan2015low  generalize variable selection methods for vector responses, but they cannot address the identifiability concern.

This section proves the following corollary.

We apply our algorithm on an equity market and a social network datasetto predict equity returns and user popularity respectively.Our baselines include ridge regression (вҖңRidgeвҖқ), reduced rank ridge regression mukherjee2011reduced  (вҖңReduced ridgeвҖқ), LASSO (вҖңLassoвҖқ), nuclear norm regularized regression (вҖңNuclear normвҖқ), reduced rank regression velu2013multivariate  (вҖңRRRвҖқ), and principal component regressionВ agarwal2019robustness  (вҖңPCRвҖқ).

Predicting equity returns. We use a stock market dataset from an emerging market that consists of approximately 3600 stocks between 2011 and 2018. We focus on predicting the next 5-day returns. For each asset in the universe, we compute its past 1-day, past 5-day, and past 10-day returns as features. We use a standard approach to translate forecasts into positionsВ ang2014asset ; zhou2014active . We examine two universes in this market: (i) Universe 1 is equivalent to S&\&P 500 and consists of 983 stocks, and (ii) Full universe consists of all stocks except for illiquid ones.

Predicting equity returns. We use a stock market dataset from an emerging market that consists of approximately 3600 stocks between 2011 and 2018. We focus on predicting the next 5-day returns. For each asset in the universe, we compute its past 1-day, past 5-day and past 10-day returns as features. We use a standard approach to translate forecasts into positionsВ ang2014asset ; zhou2014active . We examine two universes in this market: (i) Universe 1 is equivalent to S&\&P 500 and consists of 983 stocks, and (ii) Full universe consists of all stocks except for illiquid ones.

Results.  Table 1 reports the forecasting power and portfolio return for out-of-sample periods in two universes. We observe that (i) The data has a low signal-to-noise ratio. The out-of-sample R2superscriptрқ‘…2R^{2} values of all the methods are close to 0. (ii) \procвҖӢAвҖӢdвҖӢaвҖӢpвҖӢtвҖӢiвҖӢvвҖӢeвҲ’RвҖӢRвҖӢR\procрқҗҙрқ‘‘рқ‘Һрқ‘қрқ‘Ўрқ‘–рқ‘Јрқ‘’рқ‘…рқ‘…рқ‘…\proc{Adaptive-RRR} has the highest forecasting power. (iii) \procвҖӢAвҖӢdвҖӢaвҖӢpвҖӢtвҖӢiвҖӢvвҖӢeвҲ’RвҖӢRвҖӢR\procрқҗҙрқ‘‘рқ‘Һрқ‘қрқ‘Ўрқ‘–рқ‘Јрқ‘’рқ‘…рқ‘…рқ‘…\proc{Adaptive-RRR} has the smallest in-sample and out-of-sample gap (see column MSEout-in), suggesting that our model is better at avoiding spurious signals.

Predicting user popularity in social networks. We collected tweet data on political topics from October 2016 to December 2017.Our goal is to predict a userвҖҷs next 1-day popularity, which is defined as the sum of retweets, quotes, and replies received by the user. There are a total of 19 million distinct users, and due to the huge size, we extract the subset of 2000 users with the most interactions for evaluation.For each user in the 2000-user set, we use its past 5 daysвҖҷ popularity as features. We further randomly sample 200 users and make predictions for them, i.e., setting d2=200subscriptрқ‘‘2200d_{2}=200 to make d2subscriptрқ‘‘2d_{2} of the same magnitude as nрқ‘ӣn.

Results. We randomly sample users for 10 times and report the average MSE and correlation (with standard deviations) for both in-sample and out-of-sample data. In Table 2 we can see results consistent with the equity returns experiment: (i)\procвҖӢAвҖӢdвҖӢaвҖӢpвҖӢtвҖӢiвҖӢvвҖӢeвҲ’RвҖӢRвҖӢR\procрқҗҙрқ‘‘рқ‘Һрқ‘қрқ‘Ўрқ‘–рқ‘Јрқ‘’рқ‘…рқ‘…рқ‘…\proc{Adaptive-RRR} yields the best performance in out-of-sample MSE and correlation. (ii)\procвҖӢAвҖӢdвҖӢaвҖӢpвҖӢtвҖӢiвҖӢvвҖӢeвҲ’RвҖӢRвҖӢR\procрқҗҙрқ‘‘рқ‘Һрқ‘қрқ‘Ўрқ‘–рқ‘Јрқ‘’рқ‘…рқ‘…рқ‘…\proc{Adaptive-RRR} achieves the best generalization error by having a much smaller gap between training and test metrics.

We use daily historical stock prices and volumes from an emerging market to build our model. Our license agreement prohibits us to redistribute the data so we include only a subset of samples. Full datasets can be purchased by standard vendors such as quandl or algoseek. Our dataset consists of approximately 3,600 stocks between 2011 and 2018.

Universes.  We examine two different universes in this market (i) Universe 1 is equivalent to S&P 500. It consists of 800 stocks at any moment. Similar to S&P 500, the list of stocks appeared in universe 1 is updated every 6 months. A total number of 983 stocks have appeared in universe 1 at least once. (ii) Universe 2 consists of all stocks except for illiquid ones. This excludes the smallest 5% stocks in capital and the smallest 5% stocks in trading volume. Standard procedure is used to avoid universe look-ahead and survival biasВ zhou2014active .

Returns.  We use return information to produce both features and responses. Our returns are the вҖңlog-transformвҖқ of all open-to-open returnsВ zhou2014active . For example, the next 5-day return of stock iрқ‘–i is logвҒЎ(pi,t+5/pi,t)subscriptрқ‘қрқ‘–рқ‘Ў5subscriptрқ‘қрқ‘–рқ‘Ў\log(p_{i,t+5}/p_{i,t}), where pi,tsubscriptрқ‘қрқ‘–рқ‘Ўp_{i,t} is the open price for stock iрқ‘–i on trading day tрқ‘Ўt. Note that all non-trading days need to be removed from the time series pi,tsubscriptрқ‘қрқ‘–рқ‘Ўp_{i,t}. Similarly, the past 1-day return is logвҒЎ(pi,t/pi,tвҲ’1)subscriptрқ‘қрқ‘–рқ‘Ўsubscriptрқ‘қрқ‘–рқ‘Ў1\log(p_{i,t}/p_{i,t-1}).

Model.  We focus on predicting the next 5-day returns for different universes.Let рқҗ«t=(r1,t,r2,t,вҖҰ,rd2,t)subscriptрқҗ«рқ‘Ўsubscriptрқ‘ҹ1рқ‘Ўsubscriptрқ‘ҹ2рқ‘ЎвҖҰsubscriptрқ‘ҹsubscriptрқ‘‘2рқ‘Ў\mathbf{r}_{t}=(r_{1,t},r_{2,t},\dots,r_{d_{2},t}), where ri,tsubscriptрқ‘ҹрқ‘–рқ‘Ўr_{i,t} is the next 5-day return of stock iрқ‘–i on day tрқ‘Ўt.Our regression model isрқҗ«t+1=MвҖӢрқҗұt+Пө.subscriptрқҗ«рқ‘Ў1рқ‘Җsubscriptрқҗұрқ‘Ўitalic-Пө\displaystyle\mathbf{r}_{t+1}=M\mathbf{x}_{t}+\epsilon.(57)

The features consist of the past 1-day, past 5-day, and past 10-day returns of all the stocks in the same universe. For example, in Universe 1, the number of responses is d2=800subscriptрқ‘‘2800d_{2}=800. The number of features is d1=800Г—3=2,400formulae-sequencesubscriptрқ‘‘180032400d_{1}=800\times 3=2,400. We further optimize the hyperparameters k1subscriptрқ‘ҳ1k_{1} and k2subscriptрқ‘ҳ2k_{2} by using a validation set because our theoretical results are asymptotic ones (with unoptimized constants). Baseline models use the same set of features and the same hyper-parameter tuning procedure.

We use three years of data for training, one year for validation, and one year for testing.The model is re-trained every test year.For example, the first training period is May 1, 2011 to May 1, 2014. The corresponding validation period is from June 1, 2014 to June 1, 2015.We use the validation set to determine the hyperparameters and build the model, and then we use the trained model to forecast returns of equity in the same universe from July 1, 2015 to July 1, 2016. Then the model is retrained by using data in the second training period (May 1, 2012 to May 1, 2015). This workflow repeats. To avoid looking-ahead, there is a gap of one month between training and validation periods, and between validation and test periods.

We use standard approach to translate forecasts into positionsВ grinold2000active ; prigent2007portfolio ; ang2014asset ; zhou2014active . Roughly speaking, the position is proportional to the product of forecasts and a function of average dollar volume. We allow short-selling. We do not consider transaction cost and market impact. We use Newey-West estimator to produce tрқ‘Ўt-statistics of our forecasts.

We use Twitter dataset to build models for predicting a userвҖҷs next 1-day popularity, which is defined as the sum of retweets, quotes, and replies received by the user.

Data collection. We collected 15 months Twitter data from October 01, 2016 to December 31, 2017, using the Twitter streaming API. We tracked the tweets with topics related to politics with keywords вҖңtrumpвҖқ, вҖңclintonвҖқ, вҖңkaineвҖқ, вҖңpenceвҖқ, and вҖңelection2016вҖқ. There are a total of 804 million tweets and 19 million distinct users. User uрқ‘ўu has one interaction if and only if he or she is retweeted/replied/quoted by another user vрқ‘Јv. Due to the huge size, we extract the subset of 2000 users with the most interactions for evaluation.

Model.  Our goal is to forecast the popularity of a random subset of 200 users.Let рқҗІt=(y1,t,вҖҰ,yd2,t)subscriptрқҗІрқ‘Ўsubscriptрқ‘Ұ1рқ‘ЎвҖҰsubscriptрқ‘Ұsubscriptрқ‘‘2рқ‘Ў\mathbf{y}_{t}=(y_{1,t},\dots,y_{d_{2},t}), where d2=200subscriptрқ‘‘2200d_{2}=200 and yi,tsubscriptрқ‘Ұрқ‘–рқ‘Ўy_{i,t} is the popularity of user iрқ‘–i at time tрқ‘Ўt. Our regression model isрқҗІt+1=MвҖӢрқҗұt+Пө.subscriptрқҗІрқ‘Ў1рқ‘Җsubscriptрқҗұрқ‘Ўitalic-Пө\mathbf{y}_{t+1}=M\mathbf{x}_{t}+\epsilon.(58)

Features.  For each user, we compute his/her daily popularity for 5 days prior to day tрқ‘Ўt. Therefore, the total number of features is d1=2000Г—5=10,000formulae-sequencesubscriptрқ‘‘12000510000d_{1}=2000\times 5=10,000.

We remark that there are n=240рқ‘ӣ240n=240 observations. This setup follows our assumption d1вү«d2вүҲnmuch-greater-thansubscriptрқ‘‘1subscriptрқ‘‘2рқ‘ӣd_{1}\gg d_{2}\approx n.

Training and hyper-parameters. We use the period from October 01, 2016 to June 30, 2017 as the training dataset, the period from July 01, 2017 to October 30 as validation dataset to optimize the hyper-parameters, and the rest of the period, from September 10, 2017 to December 31, 2017, is used for the performance evaluation.

This paper examines the low-rank regression problem under the high-dimensional setting. We design the first learning algorithm with provable statistical guarantees under a mild condition on the featuresвҖҷ covariance matrix. Our algorithm is simple and computationally more efficient than low rank methods based on optimizing nuclear norms. Our theoretical analysis of the upper bound and lower bound can be of independent interest. Our preliminary experimental results demonstrate the efficacy of our algorithm. The full version explains why our (algorithm) result is unlikely to be known or trivial.
